2:21:1057:0:14:72:282:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:Consumption Dynamics During Recessions
2:22:1095:14:14:72:225:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:David Berger and Joseph Vavra
2:23:1124:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 20175
2:24:1152:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:May 2014
2:25:1160:14:28:72:180:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. D91,E21,E32
2:26:1179:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:27:1187:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:Are there times when durable spending is less responsive to economic stimulus? We argue that aggregate
2:28:1289:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:durable expenditures respond more sluggishly to economic shocks during recessions because microeconomic
2:29:1392:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:frictions lead to declines in the frequency of households' durable adjustment. We show this by first
2:30:1492:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:using indirect inference to estimate a heterogeneous agent incomplete markets model with fixed costs
2:31:1592:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:of durable adjustment to match consumption dynamics in PSID microdata. We then show that aggregating
2:32:1692:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:this model delivers an extremely procyclical Impulse Response Function (IRF) of durable spending
2:33:1788:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:to aggregate shocks.  For example, the response of durable spending to an income shock in 1999 is
2:34:1885:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:estimated to be almost twice as large as if it occurred in 2009. This procyclical IRF holds in response
2:35:1988:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:to standard business cycle shocks as well as in response to various policy shocks, and it is robust to
2:36:2090:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:general equilibrium. After estimating this robust theoretical implication of micro frictions, we provide
2:37:2194:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:additional direct empirical evidence for its importance using both cross-sectional patterns in PSID
2:38:2293:14:42:72:403:434:12:Times:12:Times:F:data as well as time-series patterns from aggregate durable spending.
2:39:2362:42:14:72:137:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:David Berger
2:40:2374:14:14:72:191:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:Northwestern University
2:41:2397:14:28:72:226:364:12:Times:12:Times:F:david.berger@northwestern.edu
2:42:2426:28:14:72:137:336:12:Times:12:Times:F:Joseph Vavra
2:43:2438:14:14:72:196:322:12:Times:12:Times:F:Booth School of Business
2:44:2462:14:14:72:179:308:12:Times:12:Times:F:University of Chicago
2:45:2483:14:14:72:223:294:12:Times:12:Times:F:5807 South Woodlawn Avenue
2:46:2509:14:14:72:162:280:12:Times:12:Times:F:Chicago, IL 60637
2:47:2526:14:14:72:124:266:12:Times:12:Times:F:and NBER
2:48:2534:14:0:72:229:252:12:Times:12:Times:F:joseph.vavra@chicagobooth.edu
3:49:2563:0:48:72:208:668:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:1  Introduction
3:50:2578:48:18:89:539:620:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Does the response of aggregate durable spending to a given change in policy depend on
3:51:2663:18:18:71:539:602:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the state of the business cycle? In this paper, we argue that microeconomic durable frictions
3:52:2756:18:26:71:331:584:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:lead to sluggish macro responses during recessions.
3:53:2807:26:324:193:418:558:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 1: Frequency of Durable Adjustment
3:54:2848:324:18:89:539:234:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We begin by using various data to show that while durable adjustment is always infre-
3:55:2933:18:18:71:539:216:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:quent, households are particularly unlikely to adjust their durable holdings during recessions.
3:56:3028:18:18:71:538:198:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Figure 1 shows the frequency of durable adjustment in PSID data across time.1We show
3:57:3112:18:18:71:539:180:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this both for a broad measure of durables, which is only available beginning with the PSID
3:58:3202:18:18:71:539:162:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:redesign in 1999, as well as for housing, which is available for a longer time-series.  Panel
3:59:3295:18:18:71:539:144:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:logit regressions imply that recessions lead to a decline in the probability of broad durable
3:60:3388:18:18:71:539:126:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustment of approximately 20% and a decline in the probability of buying/selling a house
3:61:3478:18:16:85:540:108:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:1See Appendix 1 for a detailed description of the data construction for these and subsequentfigures.
3:62:3578:16:12:71:539:92:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Broad durables include both housing and vehicles while housing includes only housing adjustment.  Fre-
3:63:3680:12:0:71:159:80:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:quencies are annual.
4:64:3701:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of approximately 15%.2In addition to this time-series result, wefind a strong relationship
4:65:3791:18:18:71:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:between local business cycles and durable adjustment: a two-standard deviation increase
4:66:3878:18:18:71:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in state unemployment lowers the probability of broad durable adjustment in the PSID by
4:67:3965:18:18:71:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:30%-40% after controlling for various combinations of state, year and householdfixed effects.
4:68:4058:18:18:89:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Aggregate durable turnover shows a similar pattern:  Figure 2 shows various measures
4:69:4142:18:18:71:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of durable sales in a year divided by initial stocks.  Thefirst panel shows the behavior of
4:70:4233:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:new and used vehicle sales (as measured by CNW market research) and the second panel
4:71:4317:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shows the behavior of new and existing housing sales (as measured by Census and HUD).
4:72:4402:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:While it is well-known that new durable purchases are highly cyclical, it is less widely
4:73:4490:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:documented that used durables exhibit similar patterns. These facts reinforce each other so
4:74:4581:18:18:71:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that the probability that a randomly chosen house or car changes hands falls dramatically
4:75:4670:18:20:71:142:510:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:in recessions.3
4:76:4685:20:351:134:476:490:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 2: How Frequently Does the Durable Stock Change Hands?
4:77:4746:351:16:89:539:139:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:These microeconomic adjustment patterns have important implications for business cycle
4:78:4832:16:16:85:540:123:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2See Appendix 1 for formal regression results.  Declines during recessions are highly significant and hold
4:79:4938:16:8:71:231:107:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:using various detrending procedures.
4:80:4974:8:16:85:540:99:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:3New (New+Existing) house turnover is 19% (22%) lower in recession years than non-recession years.
4:81:5072:16:12:72:540:83:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Similarly, New (New+Existing) vehicle turnover is11% (14%) lower. See Appendix 1 for description of our
4:82:5175:12:0:72:94:71:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:data.
5:83:5181:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:dynamics.  In particular, infrequent and lumpy durable adjustment at the household level
5:84:5269:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:leads aggregate durable expenditures to become much less responsive to shocks or unantici-
5:85:5359:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:pated policy changes during recessions. Why is there a cyclical link between micro lumpiness
5:86:5451:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and aggregate responsiveness?  Declines in wealth and income during recessions lead fewer
5:87:5540:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households to adjust their durable holdings upwards and more households to adjust them
5:88:5626:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:downwards.  However, the presence of depreciation means that the number of increases
5:89:5710:18:18:72:540:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:declines more quickly than the number of decreases grows.  Thus, during recessions, fewer
5:90:5799:18:18:72:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households adjust their durable holdings, which sharply reduces the elasticity of aggregate
5:91:5890:18:18:72:286:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures to aggregate shocks.
5:92:5931:18:18:89:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Understanding the behavior of broad durable expenditures is crucial for understanding
5:93:6016:18:18:72:540:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:recessions.  Consumer durables and residential investment respectively accounted for 24%
5:94:6104:18:18:72:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and 33% of the total decline in real GDP between 2007-2009 so that declines in broad durable
5:95:6196:18:17:72:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:spending account for more than half of the recession.4From 1960-2013 both components of
5:96:6283:17:18:71:539:475:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:GDP were highly cyclical and volatile, with reductions in consumer durable spending (res-
5:97:6372:18:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:idential investment) accounting for 26.6% (58.3%) of real GDP changes during recessions.5
5:98:6461:18:18:72:540:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Leamer [2007] shows that residential investment and durable spending are the two most
5:99:6546:18:18:72:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:importance components in explaining "Weakness in GDP" going into recessions prior to
5:100:6630:18:18:72:540:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2007-2009.  Thus, in a pure accounting sense, stabilizing broad durable expenditures would
5:101:6720:18:18:72:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:substantially moderate the business cycle, and indeed, a number of policy interventions
5:102:6807:18:18:72:504:367:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:during the Great Recession were specifically designed to stimulate durable demand.6
5:103:6890:18:18:89:539:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We argue for the quantitative and empirical relevance of procyclical durable responsive-
5:104:6978:18:18:71:160:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ness infive steps:
5:105:6996:18:18:89:540:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:1)  We use indirect inference to estimate a heterogeneous agent incomplete markets
5:106:7078:18:18:71:540:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model withfixed costs of durable adjustment to match household behavior in PSID.  In
5:107:7162:18:18:71:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:particular, we use a novel "gaps" based approach that maximizes thefit between model
5:108:7246:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and data along the dimensions which are most important for explaining durable adjustment.
5:109:7335:18:18:71:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:This procedure is extremely successful as our model is able to explain 72-86% of observed
5:110:7424:18:17:71:539:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:variation in household adjustment probabilities.  In addition, our estimated model matches
5:111:7514:17:18:71:314:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a variety of facts that are not directly targeted.
5:112:7564:18:18:93:539:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:2) After arguing that our estimated model matches micro consumption dynamics, we
5:113:7644:18:18:71:539:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:explore its implications for aggregate dynamics. We begin the macro analysis with a series of
5:114:7737:18:18:71:539:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate shocks in partial equilibrium. We start with a partial equilibrium analysis because
5:115:7830:18:16:85:539:134:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:4This is the change in components of real chained GDP divided by the change in total real chained GDP
5:116:7931:16:8:72:174:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:from 2007q4 to 2009q2.
5:117:7953:8:16:85:539:110:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:5This is the average contribution to percent change in real gross domestic product from BEA Table 1.1.2
5:118:8056:16:8:72:253:94:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:calculated over NBER recession quarters.
5:119:8096:8:0:85:407:86:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:6For example, the Cash for Clunkers and First Time Home Buyers credit.
6:120:8167:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:it allows us to explore a more empirically realistic baseline model and provide more sensitivity
6:121:8263:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:analysis relative to what is feasible in general equilibrium.  In addition, it allows us to
6:122:8354:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:explore the implications of business cycles for household dynamics in a model that perfectly
6:123:8446:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:replicates the aggregate behavior of income and wealth.  We show that the response of
6:124:8531:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate durable expenditures to a variety of shocks is highly procyclical. In particular, we
6:125:8625:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:allow for shocks to income, wealth, taxes, interest rates and subsidies to durable adjustment.
6:126:8719:18:18:72:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In all cases there is substantial state-dependence so that the same shock has much smaller
6:127:8809:18:18:72:435:582:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:effects if it occurs in a recession than if it occurs during an expansion.7
6:128:8884:18:18:89:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:3) As discussed above, the procyclical impulse response in our model is driven by variation
6:129:8975:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:across time in the distribution of households’ durable holdings together with the probability
6:130:9068:18:18:71:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:they adjust.  We next show that we can directly test for this reduced form implication in
6:131:9157:18:18:71:508:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:PSID data, and we show that the data strongly supports this theoretical implication.
6:132:9241:18:18:89:540:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:4) While steps 1-3 provide evidence for procyclical responsiveness in partial equilibrium,
6:133:9331:18:17:71:540:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a large literature argues that general equilibrium can undo these effects.  To assess this,
6:134:9422:17:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:we next add general equilibrium to our model and show that our conclusions are robust.8
6:135:9509:18:18:72:540:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The key reason that GE is not particularly important in our framework is that households
6:136:9597:18:18:72:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:can save in both illiquid wealth and liquid wealth.  If households can only save in only one
6:137:9689:18:18:72:540:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:asset so that=+as in Khan and Thomas [2008], then lumpy investment behavior
6:138:9767:18:18:72:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:necessarily induces violations of consumption smoothing.  With two sources of savings so
6:139:9855:18:18:72:284:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that=++this is not the case.
6:140:9889:18:18:89:540:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:5)  Finally, we show that our GE RBC model withfixed costs of durable adjustment
6:141:9969:18:18:71:540:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is a substantially betterfit to time-series evidence than are existing models with durable
6:142:10059:18:18:71:539:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:consumption. We do a much better job of matching standard business cycle moments than
6:143:10144:18:18:71:540:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:models withflexible durable adjustment.  While models with convex adjustment costs can
6:144:10230:18:18:71:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:also match these standard business cycle moments, we also show that aggregate durable
6:145:10315:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:expenditures exhibit "conditional-heteroscedasticity": they are more volatile during booms
6:146:10405:18:18:71:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:than during recessions.  Conditional heteroscedasticity arises naturally in our model with
6:147:10495:18:17:71:452:223:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:fixed costs of adjustment but not in models with convex adjustment costs.
6:148:10568:17:18:89:539:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Thus, a variety of structural, reduced-form and time-series evidence supports the conclu-
6:149:10657:18:18:71:539:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sion that durable expenditures respond less strongly to shocks during recessions.  However,
6:150:10748:18:18:71:540:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:it is important to note that our results are about the relative effectiveness of durable stimulus
6:151:10845:18:18:71:539:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:over the business cycle, so they do not on their own imply that durable stimulus is ineffective
6:152:10940:18:18:71:539:134:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:during recessions. What they do imply is that policy makers will get less bang-for-the-buck
6:153:11031:18:12:85:453:116:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:7Importantly, our model implies a state-dependent IRF but not an asymmetric IRF.
6:154:11111:12:15:85:540:104:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:8One disadvantage of GE is that the set of permissible exogneous shocks is more limited.  For example,
6:155:11213:15:12:72:539:89:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:we can no longer introduce exogenous shocks to interestrates since these are determined endogenously. For
6:156:11318:12:0:72:333:77:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:this reason, we focus on TFP shocks in general equilibrium.
7:157:11378:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:from policies designed to stabilize durable expenditures during recessions than suggested by
7:158:11470:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:linear VAR evidence.  Indeed, in Berger and Vavra [2014] we provide evidence using non-
7:159:11557:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:linear VARs that durable spending multipliers are substantially lower during recessions than
7:160:11649:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:those implied by linear VARs.  In addition, Kaplan and Violante [2014] argue that poli-
7:161:11736:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cies designed to stimulate non-durable spending are likely to become more effective during
7:162:11826:18:18:71:469:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:recessions, so such policies may be relatively more attractive for stabilization.
7:163:11907:18:18:89:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:For most of the paper, we focus on analyzing a broad measure of durable spending
7:164:11987:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that encompasses both consumer durables and housing.  We focus on this broad notion of
7:165:12073:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durables since procyclical responsiveness should apply to any purchase which is long-lived
7:166:12163:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and illiquid. These are important characteristics at the broadest level of durable aggregation.
7:167:12258:18:18:71:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In addition, both consumer durable spending and residential investment are very large and
7:168:12347:18:18:71:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:have similar cyclical patterns.9Nevertheless, focusing on this broad notion of durables
7:169:12434:18:17:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:forces us to abstract from some institutional features that may be important for housing but
7:170:12526:17:18:71:539:475:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:not for autos (or vice versa).  For this reason, we consider several robustness checks that
7:171:12617:18:18:71:524:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:focus separately on different durable components and show that our conclusions remain.
7:172:12703:18:18:89:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:There is a long line of literature studying models with durable consumption.10In pio-
7:173:12788:18:18:72:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:neering work, Eberly [1994] estimates (S,s) triggers for household auto purchases based on
7:174:12878:18:18:72:540:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the stylized model of Grossman and Laroque [1990]. She then interacts these estimated trig-
7:175:12969:18:18:72:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gers with estimates of the household wealth distribution to explain the aggregate time-series
7:176:13062:18:18:72:540:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for U.S. auto purchases.  We expand on this approach in several important ways.  Since
7:177:13148:18:18:72:540:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:her work is based on Grossman and Laroque [1990] she imposes a single (S,s) trigger.  In
7:178:13236:18:18:72:540:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:addition, she must exclude liquidity constrained households from her analysis.  We show
7:179:13323:18:18:72:540:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that in our model, which allows for binding borrowing constraints as well as (S,s) triggers
7:180:13414:18:18:72:540:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that vary with income and wealth, these assumptions matter. In contrast to our model, the
7:181:13503:18:18:72:540:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Grossman and Laroque [1990] model has very little predictive power for most households’
7:182:13590:18:18:72:540:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable adjustment. In a similar stylized model, Bar-Ilan and Blinder [1992] argue that (S,s)
7:183:13683:18:18:72:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:models should lead durable spending to depend on the past history of durable purchases and
7:184:13773:18:17:72:324:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:thus the distribution of households’ current gaps.
7:185:13823:17:16:85:539:206:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:9It is important to note that the stock of housing is somewhat larger than the stock of consumer durables,
7:186:13929:16:12:72:540:190:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:but that this is due to slightly lower depreciation rates.  The average level of real consumer durable expen-
7:187:14038:12:8:72:402:178:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:diture is slightly larger than the average level of real residential investment.
7:188:14118:8:16:81:539:170:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:10See Mankiw [1982], Bernanke [1985], and Caballero [1990] for studies of durables and the PIH hypothesis.
7:189:14224:16:12:72:540:154:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Bertola and Caballero [1990], Grossman and Laroque [1990] and Caballero [1993] provide analytical models
7:190:14328:12:12:72:539:142:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:of durable consumption withfixed costs.  Leahy and Zeira [2005], Luengo-Prado [2006], and Browning and
7:191:14430:12:12:72:540:130:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Crossley [2009] study the role of durable wealth for explaining non-durable consumption.  There is also
7:192:14533:12:12:72:540:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:a large body of work studying various aspects of durable consumption over the life-cycle including Dunn
7:193:14636:12:0:72:445:106:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:[1998], Krueger and Fernandez-Villaverde [2010], and Diaz and Luengo-Prado [2010].
8:194:14719:0:18:89:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Bajari, Chan, Krueger, and Miller [2013] usean alternative estimation procedure to try
8:195:14805:18:18:71:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to understand housing demand.   In contrast to our approach, they estimate a reduced
8:196:14889:18:18:71:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:form housing demand function and then back out utility parameters tofit these reduced
8:197:14974:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:form estimates rather than solving the households’ dynamic programming problem.  This
8:198:15059:18:18:71:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:approach makes the results less suitable for analyzing policy changes that might alter the
8:199:15149:18:18:71:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:reduced form relationship they estimate.  In addition, they only explore one-time shocks in
8:200:15240:18:18:71:474:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:partial equilibrium, in contrast to our emphasis on business cycle implications.
8:201:15320:18:18:89:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Iacoviello and Pavan [2013] build an incomplete markets model withfixed costs of housing
8:202:15408:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustment and aggregate shocks. In contrast to our paper, they perform a simple calibration
8:203:15500:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exercise for the parameters of the model and do not explore its ability to explain micro
8:204:15588:18:18:71:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:dynamics. In addition, they focus on entirely different aggregate questions. While our model
8:205:15680:18:18:71:539:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is infinite horizon, they instead build a life-cycle model, and computational considerations
8:206:15772:18:18:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:then require an annual rather than quarterly frequency.  As such, their model is less suited
8:207:15864:18:17:71:539:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for examining business cycle dynamics and they instead focus on explaining secular changes
8:208:15954:17:18:71:185:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in aggregate volatility.
8:209:15978:18:18:89:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Kaplan and Violante [2014] study the implications of illiquid wealth holdings such as
8:210:16063:18:18:71:539:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durables for the behavior of non-durable consumption and show that they are able to explain
8:211:16154:18:18:71:539:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the response of non-durable consumption to one-timefiscal rebate payments.  In addition,
8:212:16242:18:18:71:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:they briefly show that illiquidity can potentially lead to state-dependent consumption dy-
8:213:16332:18:18:71:539:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:namics. We view our work as highly complementary to their own but it is distinct in several
8:214:16423:18:18:71:539:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ways. For the most part, we focus on the implications of illiquidity for durable expenditures
8:215:16516:18:18:71:539:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rather than for non-durable spending because durable spending is substantially more impor-
8:216:16606:18:18:71:539:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tant for understanding business cycle behavior. Since our motivation is understanding how
8:217:16695:18:18:71:540:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:micro consumption dynamics influence aggregate business cycles, our model also features a
8:218:16784:18:18:71:494:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:variety of aggregate shocks and we explore the implications of general equilibrium.
8:219:16867:18:18:89:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, our paper is closely related to Caballero, Engel, and Haltiwanger [1995], Ca-
8:220:16953:18:18:71:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ballero, Engel, and Haltiwanger [1997] and Bachmann, Caballero, and Engel [2013], which
8:221:17040:18:18:71:540:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:argue for time-varying responsiveness arising from lumpyfirm behavior.  Besides the ob-
8:222:17127:18:17:71:540:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:vious difference that we study households rather thanfirms, there are several distinctions
8:223:17217:17:18:71:539:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:between our analyses.  In Caballero, Engel, and Haltiwanger [1995] and Caballero, Engel,
8:224:17305:18:18:71:539:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and Haltiwanger [1997] they impute capital and employment gaps and explore their aggre-
8:225:17392:18:18:71:539:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gate implications.  However, their imputed gaps are inconsistent with those arising under
8:226:17481:18:18:71:539:134:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:optimalfirm behavior.  For example, in Caballero, Engel, and Haltiwanger [1995] afirm’s
8:227:17568:18:18:71:540:116:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:imputed capital gap is the difference between its current capital and what it would choose in
8:228:17661:18:18:71:539:98:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a frictionless neoclassical benchmark, but that is not the optimal policy in their structural
8:229:17754:18:39:71:539:80:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model.  In contrast, our gap imputation is fully model consistent.  Bachmann, Caballero,
8:230:17842:39:0:303:309:41:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:7
9:231:17843:0:18:72:539:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and Engel [2013] build a quantitative GE model offirm investment and targets various
9:232:17927:18:18:71:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate time-series facts to address concerns that these early papers were not robust to
9:233:18017:18:18:71:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:general equilibrium and lacked quantitative realism. However, they do not test their model
9:234:18107:18:18:71:218:654:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:implications in micro data.11
9:235:18136:18:18:89:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:To summarize, while our analysis overlaps in part with many papers, we are thefirst
9:236:18219:18:18:71:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:paper to jointly explore the micro and macro implications of household durable adjustment
9:237:18308:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in an estimated, quantitative GE model.  The existing literature shows that ignoring micro
9:238:18398:18:18:71:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:facts, macro facts or general equilibrium can potentially lead one to different conclusions, so
9:239:18493:18:45:71:521:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we view the synthesis of these approaches as an important methodological contribution.
9:240:18579:45:34:72:291:519:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:2  Model and Estimation
9:241:18602:34:26:72:240:485:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.1  Model Description
9:242:18624:26:18:72:540:459:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Our baseline model for estimation is a standard incomplete markets model with the addi-
9:243:18711:18:18:72:539:441:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tion of household durable consumption subject tofixed costs of adjustment.  Households

9:245:18885:18:18:71:539:405:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idiosyncratic earnings shocks as well as borrowing constraints.  In this section, we describe
9:246:18978:18:18:71:539:387:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the partial equilibrium version of the model with no aggregate shocks, and in the following

10:289:20454:24:18:89:539:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Following Bachmann, Caballero, and Engel [2013]0≤≤1is a "required maintenance"

10:292:20706:18:18:71:539:473:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:fixing a broken furnace in a house.14When a household adjusts its durable stock, it must
10:293:20794:18:17:71:544:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:payfixed adjustment costs that take two forms.  First, they lose afixedfractionofthe
10:294:20878:17:18:71:539:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:value of their durable stock.   These costs correspond to brokers fees, titling costs, etc.
10:295:20969:18:18:71:539:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Second, households face some time cost of adjusting their durable holdings.  These costs
10:296:21057:18:18:71:539:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:correspond to, e.g., the time involved in searching for a new house or in researching which
10:297:21148:18:18:71:540:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:car to purchase. We allow for this general specification because these two adjustment costs
10:298:21239:18:18:71:540:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:may interact differently with the business cycle. The opportunity cost of time is procyclical
10:299:21332:18:18:71:539:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:so that time costs will tend to generate countercyclical durable adjustment.  Conversely,
10:300:21421:18:18:71:540:330:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:fixed costs that are proportional to the stockof durables have the most bite when income is
10:301:21512:18:18:71:539:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:low and tend to generate procyclical durable adjustment.  Estimating a specification with
10:302:21601:18:18:71:391:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:both costs allows the data to inform their relative importance.
10:303:21664:18:18:89:510:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Given these assumptions, the infinite horizon problem can be recast recursively as
10:304:21746:18:15:81:539:258:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:12Piazzesi and Schneider [2007] provides some evidence in favor of the Cobb-Douglas period utility function.
10:305:21854:15:12:72:543:243:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Note the Cobb-Douglas utility function also means we can normalize the serviceflowsfromdurablestobe
10:306:21953:12:8:72:265:231:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:equal to the stock without loss of generality.
10:307:21999:8:12:81:459:223:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:13Endogenizing hours complicates the model and does not affect our main conclusions.
10:308:22083:12:16:81:539:211:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:14In previous versions of this paper, we considered an adjustment cost function that allowed households
10:309:22186:16:12:72:540:195:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:to endogenously choose the amount of maintenance between0and1without paying thefixed adjustment
10:310:22281:12:12:72:540:183:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:cost.  This led to similar results but substantially increases the computational burden of the model, which
10:311:22388:12:0:72:194:171:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:makes estimation infeasible.

11:336:22761:33:18:89:539:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We now turn to a discussion of how we estimate the parameters of the model.  The
11:337:22841:18:39:71:400:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:computational solution of the model is discussed in Appendix 2.
11:338:22904:39:25:72:186:345:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.2  Estimation
11:339:22919:25:18:72:540:320:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:To decrease computational burden, our estimation procedure proceeds in two steps: wefirst
11:340:23008:18:18:71:539:302:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:calibrate some subset of parameters for which we have reliable external evidence.  We then
11:341:23098:18:18:71:539:284:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:estimate the remaining parameters using an indirect inference procedure, which we describe
11:342:23188:18:35:71:109:266:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shortly.
11:343:23196:35:25:71:321:231:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:2.2.1  Calibration and Model Restrictions
11:344:23237:25:18:71:539:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We calibrate several parameters of our model in standard ways but have explored the robust-
11:345:23328:18:18:71:540:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ness of our conclusions to changes in these parameters.  We set=00125, which delivers
11:346:23415:18:18:71:540:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an annual interest rate of approximately 5%, and we set the discount factor=098In
11:347:23499:18:18:71:539:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:our benchmark model we set=2.Wenormalize=1and set=13We calibrate
11:348:23568:18:18:71:539:134:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the idiosyncratic productivity process to match the persistence and variance of annual labor
11:349:23660:18:18:71:539:116:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:earnings in PSID data which yields a persistence of idiosyncratic earnings of 0.975 and a
11:350:23749:18:0:71:539:98:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:standard deviation of 0.1, and we set the payroll tax equal to 5% to reflect a combination
12:351:23841:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of the statutory rate with phaseouts for high income.15We calibrate the depreciation rate
12:352:23930:18:18:71:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of durables to match data from the BEA, weighted by the relative size of the housing and
12:353:24018:18:0:71:363:672:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f7:B:consumer durable stocks. That is, we set=
12:354:24067:0:11:363:380:679:36:g_d0_f8:36:g_d0_f8:?:
12:355:24070:11:0:337:417:668:65:g_d0_f7:145:g_d0_f5:?:++
12:356:24082:0:8:418:438:677:65:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f7:?:
12:357:24085:8:0:418:432:669:65:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f7:?:
12:358:24087:0:8:455:486:676:65:g_d0_f7:36:g_d0_f8:?:
12:359:24092:8:14:439:540:668:65:g_d0_f7:145:g_d0_f2:A:+which
12:360:24108:14:18:71:256:654:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:delivers a quarterly value of 0.018.16
12:361:24146:18:18:89:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In the general formulation of our model, durables serve a dual role: they provide direct
12:362:24234:18:18:71:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:utility to households, but they also serve as collateral against which households can borrow.
12:363:24327:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:For most of the analysis that follows, we will shut down this second channel by setting=1.
12:364:24418:18:18:71:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:However, in Appendix 4 we estimate a version of the model with=020so that households
12:365:24504:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:need only pay a 20% down payment to purchasenew durable holdings.  We show that this
12:366:24588:18:18:71:526:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:version of the model delivers similar results both for micro and macro durable dynamics.
12:367:24676:18:18:89:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:There are two main reasons that we choose to make the model with=1our benchmark:
12:368:24757:18:18:71:539:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:First, when1and there is no adjustment costs on, the model implies that households
12:369:24842:18:18:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:can costlessly adjust their durable equity.  In other words, such a parameterization implies
12:370:24934:18:17:71:540:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that households can costlessly refinance, which is clearly counterfactual.  Since it is infeasi-
12:371:25030:17:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ble to solve a more realistic model with liquid assets, semi-liquid durable equity, and illiquid
12:372:25126:18:18:71:540:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durables we concentrate on the case with no refinancing rather than the case with costless
12:373:25216:18:18:71:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:refinancing as our benchmark. Second, if collateral constraints become looser during expan-
12:374:25307:18:18:71:539:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sions this will tend to amplify all of our results since when down-payment requirements are
12:375:25398:18:18:71:539:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:low households can rapidly adjust their durable holdings in response to shocks. In contrast,
12:376:25490:18:18:71:539:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:when down-payment requirements are large, households must save a larger amount of liquid
12:377:25578:18:18:71:539:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:assets before increasing their durable holdings. By shutting this channel down, our quanti-
12:378:25669:18:18:71:539:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tative conclusions are thus relatively conservative.  Setting=1in our benchmark model
12:379:25755:18:18:71:539:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:alsomakesourresultsmorecomparabletothemodel in Kaplan and Violante [2014], which
12:380:25835:18:18:71:358:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rules out collateralized borrowing against illiquid assets.
12:381:25894:18:18:89:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In addition to exploring the role of collateral constraints, Appendix 4 also explores a
12:382:25981:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:second important empirical extension of our model.  In particular, we consider the role
12:383:26068:18:18:71:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of rental markets for our analysis and provide evidence that introducing rental markets
12:384:26155:18:18:71:540:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:has little quantitative effect on our results.   While rental markets are not particularly
12:385:26245:18:17:71:539:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:important for consumer durables, they play a large role in housing markets.   It would
12:386:26331:17:18:71:539:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:be desirable to build a model with separate consumer durables and housing, but this is
12:387:26417:18:18:71:539:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:technically infeasible. We disallow rental markets in our benchmark model for three reasons:
12:388:26509:18:16:81:539:152:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:15Since the tax isfixed across time, and hours are exogenous this plays essentially no role in our analysis.
12:389:26617:16:12:72:540:136:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Using a higher value to match overall income taxes (orexcluding taxes from the model entirely) yields
12:390:26718:12:12:72:540:124:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:nearly identical results along all dimensions.  We only include the tax so that we can perform simple policy
12:391:26826:12:8:72:426:112:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:experiments with temporary and permanent tax changes in the following section.
12:392:26904:8:16:81:539:104:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:16We have solved versions of the model with both higher and lower depreciation rates and arrived at similar
12:393:27011:16:0:72:124:88:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:conclusions.
13:394:27025:0:18:72:539:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:1) Consumer durable spending represents morethan half of total broad durable spending
13:395:27110:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:from 1960-2013, and rental markets are not important for consumer durables. 2) Introducing
13:396:27200:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rental markets increases the computational burden of the problem substantially by adding
13:397:27288:18:18:72:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an additional choice.173)  The indirect inference procedure we describe next is based
13:398:27373:18:18:71:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:on the "gap" between a households’ current durable holdings and those it would hold if it
13:399:27462:18:18:71:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:temporarily faced no adjustment costs.  Defining gaps in a world with rental markets is
13:400:27549:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:not straightforward.18Focusing on a benchmark model without rentals and restricting the
13:401:27636:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:empirical analysis to homeowners obviates all of these issues.  Nevertheless, Appendix 4
13:402:27724:18:35:71:473:564:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:shows that the introduction of rental markets does not alter our conclusions.19
13:403:27803:35:25:72:242:529:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:2.2.2  Estimation Procedure
13:404:27830:25:18:72:539:504:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The remaining parameters of our model are the proportionalfixed cost of durable adjustment,
13:405:27921:18:18:71:540:486:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:the time cost of durable adjustment, the non-durable weight in utility, and the level
13:406:28012:18:18:72:540:468:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of required maintenance. In addition, we also estimate a measurement error parameter,
13:407:28098:18:18:72:539:450:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:, which allows for all variables in the data and model to be reported with some error. We
13:408:28189:18:18:72:540:432:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:assume that the reported value of a variablebisthetruevalueplus some percentage
13:409:28270:18:18:72:359:414:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:measurement error:b=(1 +b)withb∼ (0).
13:410:28318:18:18:89:539:396:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We estimate these parameters using a "gap" based indirect inference procedure.  First
13:411:28403:18:18:71:539:378:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f13:B:note that in models withfixed adjustment costs, we can always define a gap=log∗−
13:412:28485:18:18:71:548:360:145:g_d0_f6:145:g_d0_f2:B:log(−1)where∗is the choice ofthat solves the maximization problem in.Intu-
13:413:28570:18:17:71:539:342:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:itively,measures the difference between the stock of durables that a household inherits at
13:414:28661:17:18:71:539:325:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the start of a period and the stock of durables that a household would choose if it adjusted
13:415:28753:18:18:71:539:307:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:today. However, since the household does face adjustment costs, its actual choice of durables
13:416:28846:18:18:71:540:289:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:today may or may not be equal to∗.Ifthen the household will choose
13:417:28930:18:18:72:539:271:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to adjust and set=∗and otherwise, the household will choose to not adjust and will set
13:418:29018:18:18:72:543:253:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:=−1(1−(1−))The larger the (absolute) value ofthemorelikelyitisthatthe
13:419:29094:18:18:72:540:235:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f6:B:gains from adjusting exceed thefixed adjustment cost.  Thus, the adjustment hazard()
13:420:29180:18:18:71:539:217:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:will be increasing in the (absolute) size of the gap.  This implies that measuring household
13:421:29272:18:18:71:465:199:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gaps is essential for understanding households’ durable adjustment decisions.
13:422:29349:18:18:89:539:181:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In addition, the distribution of gaps()plus the adjustment hazard()also deter-

16:573:36095:0:8:145:151:717:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C:¡
16:574:36096:8:0:152:165:709:145:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f7:?:c
16:575:36099:0:9:165:176:717:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C:¢¢
16:576:36101:9:18:181:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:collapses the time-series evolution of the joint-density ofcinto a
16:577:36169:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:one-dimensional probability of adjustment as a function of gaps.  Thus, our indirect infer-
16:578:36260:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ence estimator in essence collapses high-dimensional joint-densitiesΓ(b)to more practical
16:579:36350:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:one-dimensional functions.  Since our reduced form auxiliary model is collapsing some in-
16:580:36439:18:18:71:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:formation from the full structural model andis also introducing measurement error and
16:581:36524:18:18:71:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:time-aggregation bias, it will in general be a misspecified description of the dynamics of
16:582:36614:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the true model.  However, it is important to note that as usual in indirect inference, con-
16:583:36705:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sistent estimation does not require the auxiliary model to be correctly specified.  As long
16:584:36796:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as the reduced form model is computed identically on actual and simulated data we will
16:585:36882:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:achieve consistent estimation.  We further discuss this point in addition to a discussion of
16:586:36974:18:18:71:367:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:identification of our structural parameters in Appendix 3.
16:587:37032:18:18:89:539:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Now that we have formally stated our estimation procedure, we provide some additional
16:588:37117:18:18:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:discussion in intuitive terms before turning to results.   It is important to note that since
16:589:37210:18:17:71:539:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the distribution of gaps in the model as well as in the data are purely functions of the joint
16:590:37304:17:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:distribution of observables,b, our estimation strategy is in some sense trying to make these
16:591:37397:18:18:71:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:joint distributions line up with each other.  If the joint distribution of observables in the
16:592:37490:18:18:71:539:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:modelΓ(c)was able to perfectly match the joint distribution of observables in the data
16:593:37578:18:18:71:539:403:145:g_d0_f16:145:g_d0_f2:B:Γ(b), then by construction the distribution of gaps in the model and data would be identical.
16:594:37672:18:18:89:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:However, given that we have few parameters and thatΓ(b)is an extremely high dimen-
16:595:37756:18:18:72:540:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sional object, a perfectfit is clearly unobtainable.26Since it is infeasible to perfectly match
16:596:37851:18:18:71:539:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the joint-distribution of wealth, durable holdings and non-durable consumption, which mo-
16:597:37940:18:18:71:539:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ments of this distribution are most important to match?  Our gap-based indirect inference
16:598:38029:18:18:71:539:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:procedure provides the answer to this question.  We should weight moments ofΓ(b)by
16:599:38113:18:18:71:539:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:their importance for determining gaps.  For example, if our model told us that the ratio
16:600:38201:18:18:71:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of non-durable to durable consumption was extremely important for determining household
16:601:38288:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gaps, while liquid wealth was unimportant, then our estimation strategy would place more
16:602:38376:18:18:71:497:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:weight on matching the former distribution and less weight on matching the latter.
16:603:38458:18:17:89:539:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In the following section, we will show that our bestfit parameters yield a distribution of
16:604:38548:17:18:71:539:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gaps in the model that is an extremely goodfit to the distribution in the data, which means
16:605:38639:18:19:71:539:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we match the moments ofΓ(b)that are important for determining gaps.27More importantly,
16:606:38726:19:16:81:540:169:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:26A large literature exists just trying to match the wealth-distribution.   MatchingΓ¡¢is a vastly
16:607:38826:16:11:71:540:153:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:more difficult goal since wealth, durable and non-durable expenditures are not independent.   For ex-
16:608:38927:11:0:71:423:142:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:ample, existing studies that target thewealth distribution attempt to match
16:609:39002:0:8:429:434:150:100:g_d0_f9:100:g_d0_f9:?:R
16:610:39003:8:0:437:505:142:100:g_d0_f17:100:g_d0_f19:?:()whileΓ
16:611:39015:0:8:507:512:150:100:g_d0_f9:100:g_d0_f9:?:¡
16:612:39016:8:0:512:521:142:100:g_d0_f17:49:g_d0_f18:?:
16:613:39018:0:8:521:526:150:100:g_d0_f9:100:g_d0_f9:?:¢
16:614:39019:8:16:532:77:142:100:g_d0_f14:100:g_d0_f9:?:=R
16:615:39021:16:0:76:80:126:49:g_d0_f18:49:g_d0_f18:?:
16:616:39022:0:12:83:88:138:100:g_d0_f9:100:g_d0_f9:A:R
16:617:39023:12:0:87:91:126:49:g_d0_f18:49:g_d0_f18:A:
16:618:39024:0:12:94:99:138:100:g_d0_f9:100:g_d0_f9:?:R
16:619:39025:12:8:98:89:126:49:g_d0_f18:49:g_d0_f2:?:(  )is clearly a much more complicated object.27
16:620:39091:8:12:89:543:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:In the following section, we show that our model is a goodfit for various moments ofΓ(),whichshows
16:621:39190:12:12:71:539:106:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:that our bestfit parameters do not produce unrealistic distributions of observablesThis suggests that an
16:622:39295:12:12:72:539:94:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:alternative estimation procedure directly targetingΓ()would likely yield similar results.  However, by
16:623:39398:12:0:71:539:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:construction, such a procedure would be less accurate at predicting actual household durable adjustment
17:624:39503:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we show that our model is very accurate at predicting actual durable adjustment in the data.
17:625:39595:18:0:72:113:690:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f7:B:Since
17:626:39602:0:13:116:123:703:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:A:³
17:627:39603:13:0:123:141:690:145:g_d0_f5:65:g_d0_f7:?:
17:628:39605:0:10:143:150:703:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C:³
17:629:39606:10:0:152:160:693:145:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f7:?:b
17:630:39609:0:13:161:175:703:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C: ́ ́
17:631:39613:13:23:179:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:is the actual adjustment probability in the data for a household with
17:632:39682:23:0:72:184:667:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f7:B:imputed gapb=
17:633:39699:0:9:186:193:680:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C:³
17:634:39700:9:0:195:203:671:145:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f7:?:b
17:635:39703:0:13:204:211:680:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C: ́
17:636:39705:13:18:214:539:667:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:there is no guarantee that this empirical adjustment probability
17:637:39769:18:18:71:539:649:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:will correspond to that in the model.  This implies that calculating the empirical hazard
17:638:39858:18:18:71:540:631:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as a function of imputed durable gaps provides a test for model misspecification: if our
17:639:39946:18:18:71:539:613:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:structural model is misspecified then our imputed gapsbwill not be particularly useful
17:640:40034:18:18:71:539:595:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for explaining observed adjustment probabilities.  For example, ifwas a random uniform
17:641:40121:18:0:71:132:577:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f7:B:function,
17:642:40132:0:10:135:142:591:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C:³
17:643:40133:10:0:144:153:581:145:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f7:?:b
17:644:40136:0:14:154:161:591:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f9:C: ́
17:645:40138:14:17:165:539:577:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:would be completelyflat.  If imputed gaps are completely random then
17:646:40206:17:18:71:539:560:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households with large imputed gaps will be just as likely to adjust as households with gaps
17:647:40297:18:18:71:539:542:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of zero.  Finding an upward sloping empirical hazard as a function of (absolute) imputed
17:648:40385:18:18:71:539:524:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gaps is evidence that our model provides useful predictive power for households’ actual
17:649:40472:18:18:71:539:506:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable adjustment decisions in the data. In essence, our estimation procedure is trying to
17:650:40563:18:18:71:539:488:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:maximize the ability of our model to explain actual durable adjustment patterns but there
17:651:40652:18:18:71:333:470:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is no guarantee that we would succeed at this goal.
17:652:40703:18:18:89:539:452:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We now turn to a brief description of our data and then present results showing that our
17:653:40791:18:18:71:540:434:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model is a very goodfit for both the density of gaps and the empirical adjustment hazard
17:654:40879:18:35:71:519:416:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:while simpler existing models are unsuccessful at explaining actual durable adjustment.
17:655:40966:35:25:71:213:381:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:C:2.2.3  Data Description
17:656:40989:25:18:71:539:356:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Here we briefly describe the data and sample restrictions for our benchmark estimation. We
17:657:41079:18:18:71:539:338:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:leave a more detailed description and various robustness descriptions for Appendix 1.  Our
17:658:41169:18:18:71:539:320:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:estimation uses data from the PSID from 1999-2011. Households are interviewed every other
17:659:41258:18:18:71:539:302:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:year, and are asked a variety of questions about non-durable consumption, wealth, housing,
17:660:41348:18:18:71:539:284:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:vehicles and income. While it would be desirable to extend the analysis to data before 1999,
17:661:41440:18:18:71:540:266:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the previous PSID samples only collected foodconsumption rather than broad non-durable
17:662:41526:18:18:71:508:248:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:consumption.  In addition, vehicle data was not constructed consistently across time.
17:663:41611:18:18:89:539:230:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The value ofis the sum of all components of food consumption, utilities, transportation
17:664:41699:18:18:71:539:212:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:expenses, schooling expenses and health services.  Our measure ofis the sum of housing
17:665:41786:18:18:71:540:194:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and vehicle values andis the sum of business value, stocks, IRAs, cash and bonds minus the
17:666:41877:18:17:71:539:176:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:value of outstanding debt. Since our benchmark model does not include rental markets, we
17:667:41965:17:18:71:539:159:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:restrict our estimation to continuous home-owners in our benchmark results. In Appendix 4
17:668:42054:18:18:71:539:141:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we discuss an extension of our model to include rental markets and adjust our PSID analysis
17:669:42145:18:18:71:540:123:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:accordingly.  After constructing measures of,,andper household member we deflate
17:670:42228:18:22:71:539:105:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:nominal values using NIPA price indices, adjust for household age and remove a household
17:671:42316:22:0:72:111:83:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:patterns.
18:672:42327:0:18:72:139:708:145:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f2:C:fixed effect.28
18:673:42342:18:18:89:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We restrict our analysis to households that are in the nationally representative core
18:674:42427:18:18:71:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f5:B:sample, whose head is less than 65 years of age, and which have non-missing data on
18:675:42512:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:and.  See Appendix 1 for additional discussion of our data, cleaning procedures and
18:676:42597:18:39:71:222:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:alternative robustness checks.
18:677:42627:39:26:72:243:597:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.3  Estimation Results
18:678:42650:26:18:72:540:571:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Table 1 displays our parameter point estimates together with bootstrapped 95% confidence
18:679:42738:18:18:72:540:553:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:intervals. Our point estimate for the fraction of the value of durables lost when adjusting is
18:680:42832:18:18:72:540:535:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:0.0525. This is line with estimates of the size of realtors fees, and it is also similar to values
18:681:42930:18:18:72:539:517:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:typically used in the literature.29In the following sections, we show that thisfixed cost has
18:682:43023:18:17:71:539:499:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:important implications for aggregate dynamics.  In contrast, we estimate a negligible (and
18:683:43113:17:18:71:539:482:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:statistically insignificant) time cost of durable adjustment.  While not directly targeted, we
18:684:43207:18:18:71:539:464:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:show that the non-durable share in utility of 0.88 delivers ratios of durable to non-durable
18:685:43299:18:18:71:539:446:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:expenditures that are consistent with the data.  The point estimate for our measurement
18:686:43386:18:18:71:539:428:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:error parameter implies that measurement error is distributed mean zero with standard
18:687:43471:18:18:71:539:410:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:deviation of 8%.  This implies that a reported value will be within 5% (10%, 15%) of the
18:688:43559:18:18:71:539:392:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:true value approximately 47% (80%, 94%) of the time. Finally, our estimated maintenance
18:689:43646:18:43:71:463:374:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:parameter implies that households offset 80% of depreciation each quarter.30

18:702:44434:15:12:72:539:111:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:estimates a value of 0.06 in models of housing adjustment.  Eberly [1994] uses a transaction cost of 0.05 in
18:703:44542:12:8:72:193:99:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:her analysis of automobiles.
18:704:44570:8:16:81:539:91:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:30This relatively large maintenance value is required to explain the fact that both housing and vehicle

19:710:45112:18:18:71:539:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:addition, the estimated densities are moderately negatively skewed due to the presence of

19:713:45334:314:18:89:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 4 shows the adjustment hazard in the model and in the data.  In the model, this
19:714:45420:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is equal to the probability that a household adjusts for a given gapcNote that the hazard
19:715:45512:18:18:71:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in the model does not follow a strict (S,s) rule, jumping from 0 to 1 at some threshold. This
19:716:45605:18:18:71:540:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is because different state variables can map to the same gap so that sometimes a household
19:717:45695:18:18:71:539:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with a given gap will choose to adjust and other times it will not.32In the data, the hazard
19:718:45787:18:18:71:540:187:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is equal to the actual empirical probability that a household with an imputed gapbchooses
19:719:45878:18:18:71:539:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to adjust.  As stressed in the previous section, this is a very strong test of whether the
19:720:45968:18:14:71:539:151:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:structural model is well-specified.  If the model is very misspecified then the imputed gaps
19:721:46060:14:22:74:424:137:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f2:B:bwill have little predictive power for empirical durable adjustment.
19:722:46130:22:11:81:347:115:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:31The skewness of the gap distribution is approximately -.35.
19:723:46191:11:16:81:539:104:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:32Note that if we conditioned on all state variables rather than just the gap, households would follow a
19:724:46295:16:0:72:141:88:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:strict (S,s) rule.
20:725:46315:0:317:164:448:709:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 4: Adjustment Probabilities in Model and PSID
20:726:46367:317:18:89:539:392:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Overall, our model is extremely successful at predicting actual durable adjustment in

20:733:46777:0:12:403:407:331:36:g_d0_f22:36:g_d0_f22:A:2

20:736:46803:0:18:408:539:318:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:.  This tells us how much

20:743:47300:0:13:268:341:220:145:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f15:?:R³|()−()|
20:744:47317:13:0:304:349:207:65:g_d0_f7:145:g_d0_f5:?:()
20:745:47324:0:0:350:391:215:65:g_d0_f7:145:g_d0_f5:?:(b)b

20:747:47334:13:18:400:539:211:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:A:This tells us the average
20:748:47360:18:18:71:540:193:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:percentage deviation between the model and empirical hazards.  Wefind that the average
20:749:47446:18:16:81:539:175:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:33Clearly the standard errors for the empirical hazard are wider than those for the model but the hazard
20:750:47550:16:12:72:540:159:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:is strongly upward sloping.  Wider standard errors inthe data occur because there is some idiosyncratic
20:751:47653:12:12:72:540:147:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:adjustment in the data not explained by our model andthis "noise" interacts with sampling error in regions
20:752:47759:12:8:72:244:135:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:of the gap distribution with little mass.
20:753:47800:8:16:81:539:127:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:34We weight the deviations between(b)and(b)by(b)to account for the fact that more gap
20:754:47894:16:12:71:539:111:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:mass is close to zero than far out in the tails.  That means that we should care more about getting the
20:755:47997:12:12:71:539:99:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:hazard correct in the middle of the distribution.  If we weight all points in the hazard equally rather than

21:757:48158:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:deviation is .276 so that given a gap, we can onaverage explain 72% of the observed hazard
21:758:48248:18:18:72:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in the data.35Thus, while our model is not a perfectfit to the empirical hazard, we can
21:759:48335:18:18:72:417:672:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:explain a very large fraction of observed adjustment probabilities.36
21:760:48404:18:18:89:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:It is important to note that since we only havefive parameters, there was no guarantee
21:761:48490:18:18:71:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that any configuration of parameters would be successful at matching the reduced form
21:762:48575:18:18:71:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:hazard and density of gaps.  In this sense, the predictive power of our model is not driven
21:763:48666:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:mechanically by imputing empirical gaps from our model structure.  In Appendix 3, we
21:764:48750:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:show this more explicitly by performing an identical estimation procedure using the model
21:765:48839:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of Grossman and Laroque [1990], which has served as the basis for many existing empirical
21:766:48928:18:18:71:540:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:studies. We show there that the empirical hazard computed from imputed gaps is nearlyflat,
21:767:49018:18:18:71:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and is, if anything downward sloping.  This implies that the model actually has modestly
21:768:49106:18:18:71:539:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:negative predictive power: when the model predicts that households in the data should be
21:769:49194:18:18:71:531:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:more likely to adjust than average, they are empirically less likely to adjust than average.
21:770:49286:18:17:89:540:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Thus, we view the strong ability of our benchmark model to predict empirical adjustment
21:771:49373:17:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:patterns as its main strength: while the structure used to impute gaps is complicated, given
21:772:49465:18:18:71:495:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:our imputed gap we are highly accurate at predicting when households will adjust.
21:773:49546:18:18:89:539:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In addition to the hazard and density, which are explicitly targeted by our indirect
21:774:49630:18:18:71:544:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inference estimation procedure, we can also assess the modelfitalongvariousdimensions
21:775:49715:18:18:71:539:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:which are not directly targeted.  Kaplan and Violante [2014] emphasize the importance of
21:776:49803:18:18:71:539:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:"wealthy-hand-to-mouth" consumers for explaining household consumption dynamics. They
21:777:49888:18:18:71:539:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:argue that many households have a large fraction of their wealth in illiquid assets such as
21:778:49979:18:18:71:540:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durables and that these households may behave quite differently from those with access
21:779:50065:18:18:71:539:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to liquid wealth.   Thus, if we want to take seriously the implications of our model for
21:780:50153:18:18:71:539:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:consumption dynamics, it is important that it implies reasonable numbers of both hand-
21:781:50239:18:18:71:540:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to-mouth and wealthy-hand-to-mouth households.  We define a hand-to-mouth household
21:782:50322:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as one who has liquid assets less than one-half of their monthly labor earnings, and we
21:783:50409:18:18:71:540:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:then define a hand-to-mouth household as wealthy-hand-to-mouth if its durable holdings
21:784:50495:18:17:71:540:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:are greater than the 25th percentile of durable holdings in the population.37Using this
21:785:50582:17:18:71:540:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:definition in PSID data, 28.7% of households are hand-to-mouth and 17.8% of households
21:786:50668:18:16:81:539:188:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:35The average absolute difference (rather than percentage difference) between the model and empirical
21:787:50769:16:12:72:540:172:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:hazard is .038.  In addition, as noted in the previous footnote, we weight deviations by the density of gaps.
21:788:50878:12:12:72:540:160:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:If we instead weight all points on the hazard equallythen we explain 86% of the observed hazard in the data
21:789:50985:12:8:72:239:148:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:andfind an absolute deviation of .032.
21:790:51023:8:16:81:539:140:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:36We do not model life-cycle interactions or shocks to locational preferences that might interact with
21:791:51125:16:12:72:540:124:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:housing decisions. We suspect that the unexplained portion of durable adjustment is largely driven by these
21:792:51232:12:8:72:361:112:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:factors, which should be largely independent of the business cycle.
21:793:51299:8:16:81:539:104:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:37Using different definitions such as 1/4 of monthly earnings for hand-to-mouth or the 50th percentile for
21:794:51405:16:0:72:348:88:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:durable holdings produces similarfits between model and data.
22:795:51468:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:are wealthy-hand-to-mouth. While the estimation does not directly target these numbers it
22:796:51557:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:produces extremely similar results, with 26.4% of households hand-to-mouth and 18.0% of
22:797:51644:18:18:72:254:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households wealthy-hand-to-mouth.
22:798:51677:18:18:89:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In addition, our model produces an average frequency of adjustment which is close to that
22:799:51766:18:18:72:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in PSID data.  Using our broad definition of durables that encompasses housing+vehicles,
22:800:51854:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable stocks in the PSID data have an annual frequency of adjustment of 10.8%.  The
22:801:51939:18:26:72:468:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model implies a frequency of adjustment of only slightly above this at 12.9%.
22:802:52016:26:352:185:427:574:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 5: Durable Holdings in Model and Data
22:803:52060:352:18:89:539:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, we can assess the model’s ability to match the overall patterns of durable holdings
22:804:52152:18:18:71:547:204:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in the data. In Figure 5 we show four different slices of the durable distribution inΓ(b).We
22:805:52245:18:18:71:540:186:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:show the unconditional distribution of durable holdings as well as the relationship between
22:806:52336:18:18:71:539:168:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable holdings and non-durable consumption, the relationship between durable holdings
22:807:52423:18:18:71:539:150:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and total wealth, and the relationship between durable holdings and income.  Overall, the
22:808:52512:18:18:71:539:132:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model is a goodfit to the data.  The only place where the model misses somewhat more
22:809:52596:18:18:71:539:114:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:substantially is on the mean level of durable holdings.  While the distribution of durable
22:810:52686:18:18:71:539:96:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:holdings around the mean in the model and data are quite similar, the model overstates mean
22:811:52777:18:0:71:539:78:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable holdings relative to the data by roughly 10%. However, this does not have important
23:812:52870:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:consequences for any of our results. We can refit a version of the model that explicitly targets
23:813:52966:18:18:71:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:mean durable holdings to be equal in the model and data. By construction, this model is a
23:814:53055:18:18:71:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:slightly worsefit for the distribution of gaps and hazards but gives almost identical aggregate
23:815:53150:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:results. Again, the fact that our benchmark estimation does not exactly match mean durable
23:816:53240:18:18:71:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:holdings in the data implies that mean durable holdings are not particularly important for
23:817:53330:18:18:71:334:618:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:determining the distribution of gaps and hazards.38
23:818:53381:18:18:89:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Overall our estimated model is a goodfit to household level consumption dynamics both
23:819:53466:18:18:71:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:along targeted as well as untargeted dimensions. Bolstered by this good microeconomicfit,
23:820:53555:18:45:71:360:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we now explore the aggregate implications of our model.
23:821:53610:45:30:72:540:519:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:F:3  Aggregate Implications of Lumpy Durable Purchases
23:822:53662:30:18:72:540:489:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We explore the macroeconomic implications of our model byfirst exploring the response
23:823:53747:18:18:71:539:471:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to a number of shocks in partial equilibrium.  The use of partial equilibrium analysis has
23:824:53837:18:18:71:539:453:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:several advantages: 1) Partial equilibrium is substantially faster to compute than general
23:825:53927:18:18:71:539:435:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium, which allows us to explore the robustness of our results to various extensions such
23:826:54023:18:18:71:539:417:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as collateralized borrowing and rental markets and to perform additional sensitivity analysis.
23:827:54117:18:17:71:539:399:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2) In partial equilibrium we can explore a number of aggregate shocks (such as exogenous
23:828:54205:17:18:71:539:382:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:changes in interest rates) that are more challenging to model in general equilibrium.  We
23:829:54294:18:18:71:539:364:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:will argue that lumpy micro adjustment has important implications for how actual durable
23:830:54382:18:18:71:539:346:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:spending responds to any shock that changes desired durable holdings, so it is important to
23:831:54473:18:18:71:540:328:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:explore robustness to a variety of shocks.393) In partial equilibrium, we can pick a sequence
23:832:54566:18:18:71:539:310:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of aggregate income and wealth shocks that exactly reproduces the behavior of U.S. GDP
23:833:54652:18:18:71:539:292:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and capital across time so that our simulated economy well-approximates the actual U.S.
23:834:54739:18:39:71:117:274:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:economy.
23:835:54747:39:26:72:290:235:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3.1  Aggregate Income Shocks
23:836:54775:26:18:72:540:209:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We begin by exploring the implications of aggregate income shocks.  For brevity, we leave
23:837:54864:18:17:72:540:191:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the full model description to Appendix 2 and just discuss the changes in the model relative
23:838:54955:17:18:72:540:174:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f5:B:to the previous section.   In the previous section, we assumed thatlog0=log+
23:839:55036:18:19:72:539:156:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with∼(0)whereis an idiosyncratic income shock.   We introduce aggregate
23:840:55113:19:16:81:539:137:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:38This makes sense since as average durable holdings rise both−1and∗will tend to rise and gaps are
23:841:55213:16:12:72:540:121:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:not that affected. Furthermore, time-series movements in aggregate durable expenditures also don’t depend
23:842:55318:12:8:72:499:109:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:much on mean durable holdings since they are determined by changes inrather than levels of.
23:843:55411:8:16:81:539:101:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:39Since our mechanism applies in a wide-variety of environments and in response to a variety of shocks, we
23:844:55517:16:12:72:540:85:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:prefer to focus on documenting the generality of our mechanism rather than taking a stand on a particular
23:845:55622:12:0:72:516:73:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:source of business cycle shocks or focusing on the institutional details of one particular policy change.
24:846:55729:0:18:72:539:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:income shocks by assuming that total household wageslogare the sum of an idiosyncratic
