24:848:55864:36:26:249:363:654:145:g_d0_f6:145:g_d0_f5:C:log=log+log
24:849:55882:26:18:89:544:628:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:As before, we assume that the idiosyncratic component of income,log,followsanAR
24:850:55962:18:18:71:539:610:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:process with persistence 0.975 and standard deviation of 0.10.  We assume that the aggre-
24:851:56051:18:18:71:539:592:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gate component of income,log, follows an AR process with persistence 0.87 and standard
24:852:56138:18:18:71:540:574:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:deviation 0.008 to match the behavior of hpfiltered GDP from 1960-2013.40This adds
24:853:56220:18:18:72:540:556:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:one additional aggregate state-variable to the household’s problem but solution methods are
24:854:56311:18:18:72:540:538:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:otherwise unchanged.  We solve this model using the parameters previously estimated and
24:855:56398:18:18:72:364:520:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:then compute impulse response functions tologshocks.
24:856:56451:18:18:89:540:502:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Motivated by the evidence in Figure 1, we are particularly interested in whether micro
24:857:56537:18:18:72:539:484:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:non-linearities in durable adjustment lead durable spending to respond differently to income
24:858:56629:18:17:72:540:466:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks which occur at different points in the business cycle.   To do this, we mustfirst
24:859:56717:17:18:71:540:449:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:define booms and recessions in our model.  We match our model to U.S. data by picking
24:860:56802:18:18:71:539:431:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a particular sequence of aggregate income shocks in the modellog19601 log20134to
24:861:56891:18:18:72:540:413:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exactly reproduce hpfiltered US GDP from 1960-2013.  Given this sequence of shocks, we
24:862:56977:18:18:72:539:395:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:can then compute the impulse response of durable expenditures to anadditionalimpulse to
24:863:57064:18:18:72:540:377:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate income at each date. That is, we feed a sequence of aggregate shocks exogenously
24:864:57154:18:18:72:540:359:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:into our model for 212 quarters.  Then given the history of aggregate shocks up to each
24:865:57241:18:18:72:540:341:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:date, we compute the full impulse response function to an additional shock at that date.
24:866:57329:18:18:72:493:323:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:See Appendix 2 for additional discussion of the computation of impulse responses.
24:867:57410:18:18:89:539:305:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We summarize our state-dependent impulse response in three ways.  First, following
24:868:57492:18:18:72:539:287:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Bachmann, Caballero, and Engel [2013], we compute thefirst element of the impulse response
24:869:57582:18:18:71:540:269:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:function (IRF) for each quarter between 1960q1 and 2013q4.  This "Responsiveness Index"
24:870:57669:18:18:71:539:251:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:provides an estimate of how much durable expenditures will respond to an aggregate shock
24:871:57757:18:18:71:539:233:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to income in the quarter in which it occurs.  We are particularly interested in the IRF on
24:872:57847:18:18:71:539:215:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:impact since this has direct relevance for how durable expenditures are likely to respond
24:873:57936:18:17:71:539:197:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in the short-run to shocks or stimulus policies during recessions.  Second, we report the
24:874:58025:17:18:71:539:180:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cumulative response41of durable expenditures to the same impulse to income.  Figure 6
24:875:58110:18:18:72:540:162:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shows that measured either using either method, durable expenditures are substantially less
24:876:58201:18:18:72:318:144:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:responsive to income shocks during recessions.42
24:877:58249:18:12:81:454:126:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:40Calibrating the income shocks to labor compensation yields nearly identical results.
24:878:58335:12:16:81:539:114:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:41The cumulative response is the total area under the impulse response function from 1-8 quarters (after
24:879:58439:16:8:72:283:98:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:which the IRFs are indistinguishable from zero).
24:880:58487:8:16:81:540:90:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:42As we will show more formally when discussing whatdrives this result, this is evidence of an impulse
24:881:58589:16:0:71:540:74:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:response that depends on the state of the business cycle, it is not evidence of an asymmetric response to
25:882:58696:0:335:119:491:709:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 6: How Responsive Are Durable Expenditures to Income Shocks?
25:883:58763:335:18:89:539:374:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:On average, the IRF on impact in recessions is only 54% of that in expansions, indicating
25:884:58852:18:18:71:540:356:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an economically significant amount of state-dependence.   Table 2 shows that the 95th
25:885:58937:18:18:71:539:338:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:percentile of the IRF on impact is 174% larger than the 5th percentile and that the 95th
25:886:59025:18:27:71:433:320:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:percentile of the cumulative IRF is 46% larger than the 5th percentile.

25:901:59402:25:21:89:539:104:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The third way we examine the extent of state-dependence is by plotting the entire impulse

26:904:59641:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:response function for particular dates.  The years 1999 and 2009 are boom and recession

26:906:59815:18:27:72:140:672:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:these years:43

26:910:59999:18:17:71:539:270:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as that in 2009.  While the IRF on impact is most relevant for assessing the short-run
26:911:60085:17:18:71:539:253:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:impact of economic shocks during recessions, these differences persist for several quarters:
26:912:60177:18:18:71:436:235:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the cumulative IRF in 1999 is more than 30% larger than that in 2009.
26:913:60246:18:18:89:539:217:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Before turning to an explanation for this procyclical durable spending IRF, we show that
26:914:60334:18:18:71:539:199:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the same result holds for a variety of other aggregate shocks. Beyond just providing a simple
26:915:60427:18:18:71:539:181:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:robustness check, this is important because we want to argue that the aggregate implications
26:916:60519:18:18:71:539:163:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of lumpy micro adjustment apply to a wide-class of aggregate shocks. Essentially all shocks
26:917:60610:18:18:71:465:145:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that are commonly used to explain business cycles yield similar implications.
26:918:60687:18:0:81:320:127:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:43Other boom and recession years yield similar results.
27:919:60744:0:26:72:290:708:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3.2  Aggregate Wealth Shocks
27:920:60772:26:18:72:540:682:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:While we consider income shocks to be the most natural proxy for U.S. business cycles in a
27:921:60862:18:18:72:540:664:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:partial equilibrium model, we next show that wealth shocks deliver similar results. We think
27:922:60954:18:18:72:540:646:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of these shocks as proxying for declines in stock market value or other asset holdings during
27:923:61047:18:18:72:539:628:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:recessions which will affect households’ consumption decisions. We assume that households’
27:924:61137:18:18:71:539:610:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:liquid wealth is subject to aggregate shocks which follow some AR process in logs.  That
27:925:61225:18:18:71:539:592:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is,0=0∗0withlog0=log+We calibrate these shocks to match
27:926:61302:18:18:72:540:574:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the persistence and standard deviation of the hpfiltered quarterly U.S. capital stock, which
27:927:61394:18:18:71:539:556:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we construct using a perpetual inventory method as in Bachmann, Caballero, and Engel
27:928:61478:18:17:71:539:538:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:[2013]. This yields a quarterly persistence of 0.95 and a standard deviation of 0.003 so that
27:929:61571:17:27:71:358:521:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate wealth shocks are small but highly persistent.
27:930:61627:27:334:153:458:494:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 9: How Responsive Are Durables to Wealth Shocks?
27:931:61682:334:18:89:539:160:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 9 shows that the durable response to wealth shocks is even more procyclical than
27:932:61769:18:18:71:539:142:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the response to income shocks.44Table II shows that the 95th percentile of the IRF on
27:933:61854:18:18:71:539:124:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:impact is more than 6 times as large as the 5th percentile.  The 95th percentile of the
27:934:61941:18:16:81:539:106:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:44Note that the model business cycles in the two versions of the model are not identical, since in one
27:935:62043:16:12:72:539:90:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:aggregate income exactly matches U.S. GDP, in the other aggregate wealth exactly matches U.S. capital.
27:936:62145:12:0:72:493:78:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Solving a model with both shocks simultaneously would be much more computationally difficult.
28:937:62240:0:18:72:409:708:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:cumulative IRF is almost 5 times larger than the 5th percentile.45
28:938:62306:18:18:89:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our baseline wealth shock is a proportionate equal decline in all households wealth so
28:939:62392:18:18:71:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that all households face the same shock. However, rich households have a greater proportion
28:940:62483:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of their total wealth in liquid assets and so are more affected by these shocks. Nevertheless,
28:941:62577:18:18:71:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this proportional shock may still understate distributional effects of wealth shocks if rich
28:942:62669:18:18:71:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households hold assets which are riskier and lose more value during recessions.  To assess
28:943:62759:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the importance of this channel, we have resolved a version of the model with wealth shocks
28:944:62849:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that only affect wealthy households as well as with wealth shocks that are increasing in the
28:945:62941:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:level of household wealth.  For brevity we do not plot the results but note that all of our
28:946:63032:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:conclusions are strengthened under these alternative specifications: if wealth shocks mainly
28:947:63124:18:39:71:386:528:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:affect the rich then the IRF becomes even more procyclical.46
28:948:63185:39:25:72:205:489:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3.3  Policy Shocks
28:949:63203:25:18:72:540:464:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In addition, we can compute impulse responses to shocks that roughly correspond to various
28:950:63293:18:18:72:540:446:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:policy experiments.  Since we do not think the business cycle is primarily driven by any
28:951:63381:18:18:72:539:428:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of these policy experiments, we now perform a slightly different experiment.  Rather than
28:952:63470:18:18:72:540:410:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:assuming that there are stochastic shocks to policy and picking these shocks to match the
28:953:63559:18:18:72:540:392:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:behavior of GDP, we introduce one-time unanticipated policy shocks on top of our previous
28:954:63648:18:18:72:540:374:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model with aggregate income shocks.  That is, we assume that households are subject to
28:955:63734:18:18:72:540:356:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate income shocks which, as before, are picked to match the behavior of U.S. GDP.
28:956:63821:18:18:72:540:338:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We then compute the optimal response of households to a one-time unanticipated policy
28:957:63906:18:18:72:508:320:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:experiment at different points in the business cycle (as defined by aggregate income).
28:958:63992:18:18:89:539:302:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:While it is not computationally feasible to simultaneously introduce stochastic policy
28:959:64078:18:18:71:539:284:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks together with stochastic aggregate income shocks, we can compute the durable re-
28:960:64165:18:18:71:539:266:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sponse to changes in policy that are either completely temporary or are fully permanent.
28:961:64253:18:17:71:540:248:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:For brevity we only report results for permanent policy shocks, but temporary shocks de-
28:962:64341:17:18:71:539:231:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:liver similar time variation.  We compute the impulse response to three policy shocks: a
28:963:64429:18:18:71:539:213:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:permanent decline in the interest rate, a permanent decline in the payroll tax, and a subsidy
28:964:64522:18:18:71:539:195:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to durable adjustment (which isfinanced by an increase in taxes).47We view these policy
28:965:64609:18:18:71:539:177:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:experiments as rough approximations to the various stimulus policies such as reductions in
28:966:64699:18:16:81:539:159:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:45Wealth shocks induce greater time-series variationin IRFs because they are more persistent than income
28:967:64803:16:8:71:408:143:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:shocks and lead to larger movements in households desired durable holdings’.
28:968:64879:8:16:81:539:135:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:46This is because as we show shortly, in a model with liquidity constraints but no illiquid wealth, the
28:969:64982:16:11:72:539:119:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:IRF is mildly countercyclical.  Since this countercyclical effect of liquidity constraints is entirely driven by
28:970:65094:11:12:72:540:108:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:households close to the liquidity constraint, if these constrained households do not face wealth shocks then
28:971:65202:12:9:72:346:96:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:this effect is shut down and the IRF becomes more procyclical.
28:972:65264:9:0:81:436:87:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:47In the modeling appendix we describe each of these experiments in more detail.
29:973:65346:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:payroll taxes and "Cash-for-Clunkers" that were implemented during the recession of 2007-
29:974:65435:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2009. While we believe a more detailed quantitative study of these particular policies is an
29:975:65527:18:18:72:544:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:importantsubjectforfutureresearch,inthispaperwewanttofocusonthebroadfactthat
29:976:65603:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:micro-level household behavior has important implications for a broad variety of aggregate
29:977:65693:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks, which necessitates abstracting from some of the institutional details important to
29:978:65783:18:24:72:182:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:each of these policies.
29:979:65806:24:333:187:424:594:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 10: Impulse Response to Policy Shocks
29:980:65850:333:18:89:539:261:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 10 plots the impulse response to each of these three policy shocks. Again, the IRF
29:981:65939:18:18:71:539:243:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is procyclical.  Table II shows that across time, the 95th percentile of the IRF on impact is
29:982:66032:18:38:71:539:225:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:60-129% larger than the 5th percentile for the interest rate, tax and durable subsidy shock.
29:983:66124:38:26:72:246:187:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3.4  Robustness Results
29:984:66147:26:18:72:540:161:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The previous sub-sections show that in response to a variety of aggregate shocks, durable ex-
29:985:66240:18:18:72:543:143:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:penditures exhibit strongly procyclical impulse response functions. Thisconclusionishighly
29:986:66330:18:18:71:539:125:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:robust to a number of model extensions.  As previously discussed, our benchmark analysis
29:987:66418:18:18:71:540:107:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:focuses on the broadest interpretation of durables withfixed adjustment costs. Nevertheless,
29:988:66510:18:18:71:539:89:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this forces us to abstract from features that may make housing respond differently to shocks
29:989:66602:18:0:71:540:71:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:than automobiles or other consumer durables.  The use of partial equilibrium simplifies
30:990:66691:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the computation of the model so that it is feasible to explore some of these questions.  In
30:991:66782:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Appendix 3, we introduce rental markets and collateralized borrowing into our model and
30:992:66869:18:18:72:507:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:show that the model continues to deliver a quantitatively significant procyclical IRF.
30:993:66955:18:18:89:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In addition, Section 5 introduces general equilibrium into our benchmark model and
30:994:67037:18:57:72:288:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shows that results continue to go through.
30:995:67079:57:28:72:540:579:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:F:4  Understanding Procyclical IRFs: Fixed Costs and
30:996:67129:28:34:101:341:551:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:Cross-Sectional Implications
30:997:67157:34:25:72:297:517:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:4.1  Importance of Fixed Costs
30:998:67187:25:18:72:540:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Why is the IRF of durable expenditures to aggregate shocks procyclical?  These aggregate
30:999:67275:18:18:72:539:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:patterns arise because of the household-level non-linearities induced byfixed costs of durable
30:1000:67369:18:18:71:539:456:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustment.   Wefirst show this by documenting that the procyclical impulse response
30:1001:67453:18:18:71:539:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:disappears when durable adjustment is frictionless.  We then discuss the microeconomic
30:1002:67539:18:18:71:539:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:mechanism that drives our result and provide additional evidence for this channel by further
30:1003:67631:18:18:71:203:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exploiting our PSID data.
30:1004:67656:18:18:89:539:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 11 shows the impulse response to income shocks in a model which is otherwise
30:1005:67739:18:18:71:539:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:identical to our benchmark model but with≡≡0.   Clearly there is much less
30:1006:67817:18:18:72:539:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:variation in impulse responses across time than in the model withfixed costs. Furthermore,
30:1007:67907:18:18:71:539:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:what variation there is now countercyclical instead of procyclical.   The reason the IRF
30:1008:67995:18:18:71:539:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:becomes countercyclical when there are nofixed costs of adjustment is that during recessions,
30:1009:68088:18:17:71:539:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:more households are close to the borrowing constraint, which increases the response of their
30:1010:68180:17:18:71:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures to income shocks. This is just a manifestation of the classic result that
30:1011:68274:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:marginal propensities to consume out of income shocks are larger for liquidity constrained
30:1012:68364:18:18:71:130:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households.
30:1013:68375:18:18:89:539:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:This experiment with nofixed costs of adjustment is important because it shows that
30:1014:68458:18:18:71:539:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:our results are driven byfixed costs rather than just by the sequence of aggregate shocks.
30:1015:68548:18:18:71:540:187:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In a model with incomplete markets, state-dependent IRFs could arise even withoutfixed
30:1016:68634:18:18:71:539:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:costs of adjustment as the business cycle interacts with borrowing constraints.  Indeed, we
30:1017:68725:18:18:71:539:151:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:find evidence of this effect, but it works in the opposite direction of our headline result and
30:1018:68820:18:0:71:160:133:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is relatively mild.
31:1019:68841:0:336:85:526:709:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 11: Impulse Response to 1% Income Shocks (Frictionless Durable Adjustment)
31:1020:68922:336:26:72:321:373:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:4.2  The Role of the Cross-Section
31:1021:68956:26:18:72:539:347:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Thus, in the model with nofixed costs of adjustment, which is inconsistent with micro data,
31:1022:69047:18:18:72:540:329:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the IRF is mildly countercyclical.  In contrast, in our benchmark model withfixed costs,
31:1023:69135:18:18:72:540:311:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that matches micro data, there is an extremely procyclical IRF.  Why dofixed costs of
31:1024:69220:18:18:72:540:293:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustment induce a procyclical IRF?  We can see this by returning to the expression for
31:1025:69308:18:0:72:264:275:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f6:B:aggregate durable investment:=

31:1028:69386:18:18:71:539:257:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to adjust their durable holdings and the larger the size of the gaps, the more responsive will
31:1029:69480:18:18:71:539:239:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:be aggregate durable investment. Caballero and Engel [2007] show that this formula can be
31:1030:69569:18:18:71:539:221:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:used to calculate the response of the economy on impact to aggregate shocks. In particular,

32:1051:70008:0:313:139:471:709:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 12: Model Gap Distribution and Hazard: Boom Vs. Bust
32:1052:70067:313:46:281:330:396:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 13
32:1053:70076:46:18:89:539:350:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 13 plots the distribution of durable gaps and adjustment hazard in a boom and
32:1054:70160:18:18:72:539:332:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in a recession, for the model with aggregate income shocks.48On average the distribution
32:1055:70248:18:18:72:540:314:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:has negative skewness because depreciation means that more households want to increase
32:1056:70334:18:18:72:540:296:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:than to decrease durable holdings.  This becomes more pronounced during the boom, as
32:1057:70418:18:18:72:540:278:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households’ desired durable holdings rise and the distribution of durable gaps shifts to the
32:1058:70510:18:17:72:539:260:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:right.49As more households are now further from their desired level of durables, they move
32:1059:70600:17:18:71:539:243:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:into the region with a higher probability of adjustment, and since all households that adjust
32:1060:70693:18:18:71:539:225:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:will respond to aggregate shocks, aggregate durable expenditures become more responsive
32:1061:70780:18:18:71:539:207:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to these shocks.  This is amplified by the increase in the probability of adjustment during
32:1062:70871:18:18:71:539:189:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a boom.  Households are more likely to adjust to a given durable gap during a boom than
32:1063:70958:18:18:71:539:171:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:during a recession as thefixed costs of durable adjustment represent a smaller fraction of
32:1064:71048:18:16:71:165:153:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:household income.
32:1065:71065:16:15:81:539:137:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:48Note that here we are plotting the true model hazards and gaps (with no measurement error) while
32:1066:71163:15:12:72:540:122:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Figure 5 plots the distribution and hazard for model data with measurement error.  While the true hazard
32:1067:71267:12:12:72:540:110:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:is zero when the durable gap is equal to zero, measurement error leads the measured hazard to be strictly
32:1068:71372:12:8:72:164:98:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:positive at all points.
32:1069:71395:8:16:81:539:90:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:49The model with business cycles driven by aggregate wealth shocks delivers stronger movements in the
32:1070:71496:16:0:72:335:74:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:distribution of gaps since wealth shocks are more persistent.
33:1071:71559:0:18:89:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Note that this increase in responsiveness issymmetric in the sign of the aggregate shock.
33:1072:71648:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:During booms, a shock that increases households’ desired durable holdings will raise aggre-
33:1073:71739:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gate durable expenditures by more than if this same shock occurs in a recession.  But it is
33:1074:71830:18:18:72:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:also true that during booms, a shock that lowers households’ desired durable holdings will
33:1075:71920:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:lower aggregate durable expenditures by more than if the same shock occurs in a recession.
33:1076:72010:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Our model implies an IRF that depends on the state of the business cycle; it does not imply
33:1077:72101:18:18:72:540:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f6:B:an asymmetric IRF.  Together the rightward shift of()and the vertical shift in()
33:1078:72185:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:greatly amplify the response of aggregate durable expenditures to any shock that changes
33:1079:72273:18:23:71:250:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:households’ desired durable stocks.

35:1117:74703:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rental markets and collateralized borrowing.  Since changing the structural model changes
35:1118:74792:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:both our parameter estimates as well as the imputed gaps in the data, our estimates of
35:1119:74878:18:18:72:539:672:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:(b)and(b)are slightly different in these alternative specifications.  Nevertheless, we
35:1120:74972:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:show that we againfind shifts in the distribution and hazards, as well as time-variation in
35:1121:75063:18:45:71:517:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the implied impulse response on impact, that conform with our theoretical predictions.
35:1122:75149:45:30:72:401:591:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:5  Robustness to General Equilibrium
35:1123:75185:30:18:72:540:561:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:There is a large and important literature studying the role of general equilibrium in models
35:1124:75277:18:18:72:540:543:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of lumpyfirm investment. In an extremely influential paper Khan and Thomas [2008] show
35:1125:75363:18:18:72:540:525:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that general equilibrium can eliminate the aggregate effects of micro lumpiness that had been
35:1126:75456:18:18:72:540:507:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:found in earlier partial equilibrium work such as Caballero, Engel, and Haltiwanger [1995].
35:1127:75547:18:18:72:540:489:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Given that our evidence thus far is purely partial equilibrium, it is important to explore
35:1128:75637:18:18:72:539:471:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:whether a similar effect arises in our model.   Does the inclusion of general equilibrium
35:1129:75726:18:18:71:540:453:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:price movements eliminate the time-varying IRF that wefind in partial equilibrium?  In
35:1130:75812:18:18:71:539:435:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this section we provide evidence that it does not, and we provide intuition for why general
35:1131:75903:18:18:71:539:417:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium is less important for lumpy household durable adjustment than is often found
35:1132:75991:18:17:71:209:399:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for lumpyfirm investment.
35:1133:76016:17:18:89:539:382:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our general equilibrium model is identical to our benchmark partial equilibrium model,
35:1134:76102:18:18:71:539:364:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:but we now endogenize the aggregate wage and interest rate.  To ease comparison of our
35:1135:76188:18:18:71:539:346:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model’s aggregate dynamics with those in the existing literature, we focus on an RBC version
35:1136:76280:18:18:71:539:328:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of the model with aggregate TFP shocks, and we forecast interest rates and wages using
35:1137:76368:18:30:72:284:310:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the methods in Krusell and Smith [1998].
35:1138:76408:30:18:89:540:280:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:A representativefirm rents capital and labor and itsfirst order conditions pin down these
35:1139:76497:18:51:71:104:262:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:prices:
35:1140:76504:51:21:234:366:211:145:g_d0_f5:65:g_d0_f7:?:=(1−)1−

37:1193:77889:33:17:89:539:424:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Where possible, we choose all parameters in the general equilibrium model to be identical
37:1194:77978:17:18:71:539:407:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to those in our benchmark estimation, but there are several new parameters and restrictions
37:1195:78069:18:18:71:539:389:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f5:B:imposed by general equilibrium.  Since the interest rate is endogenous, we now choose
37:1196:78155:18:18:71:554:371:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to target the steady-state interest rate used in partial equilibrium:=0125.Wepick
37:1197:78238:18:18:71:540:353:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:=022to match the average ratio of investment to capital.53We choose a capital share
37:1198:78324:18:18:71:508:335:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of=03, and we pick=095and=008to match the behavior of U.S. TFP.
37:1199:78395:18:18:89:539:317:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We solve the model by conjecturing an aggregate law of motion, approximating the value
37:1200:78481:18:18:72:540:299:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:function by linearly interpolating54between continuous grid points, solving the contraction,
37:1201:78573:18:18:71:539:281:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:simulating the household problem and updating the aggregate law of motion until conver-
37:1202:78660:18:18:71:539:263:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:gence is obtained.  In equilibrium, the aggregate law of motion is highly accurate.  See
37:1203:78748:18:18:71:367:245:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Appendix 2 for additional details on the solution method.
37:1204:78805:18:18:89:539:227:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:As is typical in general equilibrium models, there are now fewer degrees of freedom along
37:1205:78894:18:18:71:539:209:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:which we can add shocks to the model, so the experiments we can perform are simpler in
37:1206:78980:18:18:71:539:191:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:nature.  Since income and wealth are now endogenous, we can no longer directly introduce
37:1207:79068:18:17:71:539:173:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate shocks to these variables.  Instead, we focus on the response of durable expendi-
37:1208:79159:17:18:71:539:156:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tures to the exogenous TFP shocks in our model.  We do this not because we want to take
37:1209:79246:18:12:81:394:138:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:53Changingto higher or lower values does not affect our conclusions.
37:1210:79316:12:16:81:539:126:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:54We have found that linear interpolation gives speed advantages that make it attractive relative to cubic
37:1211:79422:16:12:72:540:110:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:spline or other interpolation methods. While linear interpolation will introduce kinks into the value function,
37:1212:79533:12:12:72:540:98:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:we do not rely on derivative based methods for solving the household problem, so this does not prove
37:1213:79633:12:0:72:180:86:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:particularly problematic.
38:1214:79660:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:afirm stand on TFP shocks as the most important driver of U.S. business cycles but rather
38:1215:79749:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for illustrative simplicity.  In the partial equilibrium section of the paper we showed that
38:1216:79841:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:our results apply to a large variety of aggregate shocks and we simply want to argue that
38:1217:79930:18:27:72:361:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:general equilibrium does not undo our basic conclusions.
38:1218:79986:27:14:72:540:627:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Figure 16: How Responsive are Durable Expenditures to TFP Shocks in General Equilib-
38:1219:80070:14:335:72:102:613:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rium?
38:1220:80075:335:18:89:539:278:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Just as in partial equilibrium, wefind a quantitatively large procyclical IRF. Figure 16
38:1221:80163:18:17:71:539:260:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shows that there is large and procyclical variation in the IRF across time. It is worth noting
38:1222:80257:17:18:71:539:243:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that movements in the IRF in this version of the model do not line up quite as sharply with
38:1223:80348:18:18:71:540:225:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:recessions as in Figure 6. However, recall that we are feeding very different aggregate shocks
38:1224:80442:18:18:71:539:207:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:into these two models.  In Figure 6, we were hitting the economy with aggregate income
38:1225:80528:18:18:71:539:189:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks that exactly correspond to actual U.S. GDP, while in Figure 16 we are hitting the
38:1226:80616:18:18:71:539:171:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:economy with TFP shocks that correspond to U.S. Solow Residuals. Since TFP in the data
38:1227:80702:18:18:71:539:153:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:does not perfectly comove with GDP, it is not surprising that the resulting IRF would line
38:1228:80792:18:18:71:539:135:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:up less sharply with observed recessions. Nevertheless, our general conclusion remains: after
38:1229:80885:18:18:71:539:117:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sequences of TFP shocks that increase household income and wealth, durable responsiveness
38:1230:80974:18:18:71:96:99:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rises.
38:1231:80980:18:0:89:540:81:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Why does the addition of general equilibrium have little effect for aggregate dynamics in
39:1232:81071:0:18:72:539:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:our environment while it has large effects in Khan and Thomas [2008]? The main reason is
39:1233:81159:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:because in our model, households have two sources of savings: households can save in liquid
39:1234:81250:18:18:72:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:assetsor illiquid assetsIn contrast, in Khan and Thomas [2008] households only have
39:1235:81336:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:access to savings through.  Khan and Thomas [2008] argue that the main reason general
39:1236:81422:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium is so important in their model is because of household consumption smoothing
39:1237:81510:18:18:72:539:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:motives.  If lumpy investment at thefirm level causes aggregate investment in capital to
39:1238:81598:18:18:72:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:move differently than in a frictionless RBC model, the representative household would face
39:1239:81688:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:more consumption volatility. That is because in their model,=+so a large change in
39:1240:81775:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:necessitates a large change inSince households have a strong consumption smoothing
39:1241:81861:18:18:72:540:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:motive, there are then large price movements in general equilibrium that undo the partial
39:1242:81950:18:18:72:277:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium effects of lumpy investment.
39:1243:81990:18:18:89:539:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In contrast, in our model=++In this environment, if lumpy durable
39:1244:82062:18:17:72:540:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustment induces aggregate dynamics forthat depart from the frictionless model, these
39:1245:82151:17:18:71:540:475:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:changes can be absorbed bywithout implying a more volatile consumption process. That
39:1246:82237:18:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is, with multiple sources of savings, large changes in the behavior of some component of
39:1247:82325:18:18:71:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:savings do not necessarily imply that households must violate consumption smoothing. This
39:1248:82414:18:18:71:539:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is similar to the intuition in Bachmann and Ma [2013] who argue that the presence of
39:1249:82498:18:18:71:539:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inventories in a model with lumpy investment reduces the importance of general equilibrium
39:1250:82588:18:45:71:106:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:effects.
39:1251:82596:45:42:72:283:340:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:6  Time-Series Evidence
39:1252:82619:42:18:72:540:298:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In this section we argue that time-series data on durable spending provides additional support
39:1253:82713:18:18:72:539:280:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for our theoretical model withfixed costs of durable adjustment.  Wefirst show that the
39:1254:82800:18:18:72:540:262:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model withfixed costs of durable adjustment delivers standard business cycle moments that
39:1255:82889:18:18:72:539:244:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:betterfit the data than a frictionless model with durable consumption. Since these moments
39:1256:82979:18:18:72:540:226:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:do not condition on the state of the business cycle, we refer to our model as better matching
39:1257:83072:18:18:72:545:208:145:g_d0_f25:145:g_d0_f2:B:unconditionalbusiness cycle moments.  While the frictionless model is not a goodfitto
39:1258:83157:18:18:71:539:190:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the data, it is straightforward to introduce convex adjustment costs into an RBC model
39:1259:83243:18:18:71:540:172:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to perfectly match the unconditional behavior of the model withfixed adjustment costs.
39:1260:83329:18:17:72:540:154:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:However, we next show that even though an RBC model with convex adjustment costs and a
39:1261:83415:17:18:72:540:137:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model withfixed costs of adjustment have observationally equivalent unconditional behavior,
39:1262:83506:18:18:71:539:119:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:they have very different implications for theconditionalbehavior of durable spending over
39:1263:83595:18:18:71:540:101:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the business cycle and that U.S. time-series data strongly supports the model withfixed
39:1264:83682:18:0:71:99:83:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:costs.
40:1265:83690:0:18:89:539:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Table 3 reports the unconditional business cycle moments from our model and how they
40:1266:83774:18:18:71:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:compare to data.55In addition, we report results for representative agent RBC models
40:1267:83858:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with and without convex adjustment costs, which we describe in Appendix 5.  Clearly, the
40:1268:83946:18:18:72:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:representative agent model with frictionless durable adjustment is a poorfit to the data.
40:1269:84035:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The volatility of both capital investment and durable spending are substantially too large
40:1270:84125:18:32:72:372:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:while the volatility of non-durable consumption is too low.
40:1271:84184:32:18:286:323:586:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Table 3

40:1273:84241:20:18:224:464:548:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Data  RBC  RBC W/ Adj  W/ Fixed Costs
40:1274:84278:18:18:147:403:530:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Durable3.04   19.56  2.582.58
40:1275:84307:18:18:147:403:512:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Non-Durable  0.57   0.41   0.630.68
40:1276:84342:18:23:147:403:494:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Investment    2.24   8.16   2.362.36
40:1277:84378:23:18:89:539:471:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The reason that investment in the frictionless RBC model is too volatile is because this
40:1278:84466:18:18:71:540:453:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model features the comovement problem identified in Greenwood and Hercowitz [1991] and
40:1279:84552:18:17:71:539:435:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:further explored in Fisher [1997].  A change in productivity changes the relative returns to
40:1280:84644:17:18:71:539:418:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:saving in productive capital vs durables. An increase in productivity makes it more valuable
40:1281:84736:18:18:71:539:400:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to shift saving into productive capital, and the additional output produced can later be
40:1282:84824:18:18:71:540:382:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:used tofinance durable consumption. This generates a strong negative correlation between
40:1283:84912:18:18:71:539:364:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures and investment in productive capital in the models with no adjustment
40:1284:85002:18:18:71:539:346:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:costs and increases the volatility of both variables.  The introduction of adjustment costs
40:1285:85093:18:18:71:539:328:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:breaks this comovement problem and substantially dampens the volatility of investment.
40:1286:85179:18:18:71:540:310:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In addition,fixed costs of adjustment make a fraction of household wealth illiquid, which
40:1287:85268:18:18:71:540:292:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:amplifies the volatility of non-durable consumption for the reasons explored in Kaplan and
40:1288:85358:18:18:71:151:274:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Violante [2014].
40:1289:85374:18:18:89:540:256:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The poorfit of frictionless multisector RBC models is well-known, so it is not surprising
40:1290:85463:18:18:71:539:238:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that we reach a similar conclusion. Moreover, quadratic adjustment costs can substantially
40:1291:85553:18:18:71:540:220:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:improve thefit of the representative agent model.56The third column of Table 3 shows that
40:1292:85642:18:17:72:540:202:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we can pick adjustment costs in an RBC model to generate exactly the same volatility of in-
40:1293:85733:17:16:81:539:185:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:55See Appendix 1 for data definitions.  We define durable expenditures as NIPA durable expenditures +
40:1294:85834:16:12:71:539:169:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:residential investment.  The BEA treats durable and residential investment differently, including housing
40:1295:85939:12:12:71:539:157:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:services in GDP while excluding durable services.  In both our model and data analysis, we define GDP
40:1296:86040:12:12:71:539:145:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:as consumer durable expenditures + private domestic investment + non-durable expenditures (excluding
40:1297:86140:12:8:71:147:133:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:housing services).
40:1298:86158:8:16:81:539:125:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:56Smooth adjustment costs can be microfounded in various ways:  Gomme, Kydland, and Rupert [2001]
40:1299:86255:16:12:72:540:109:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:add time-to-build to a disaggregated model while Davis and Heathcote [2005] introduce afixed factor of
40:1300:86357:12:0:72:122:97:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:production.
41:1301:86370:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:vestment and durable spending as in the model withfixed costs of adjustment.57This shows
41:1302:86458:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that while adjustment costs are important for matching the volatility of durable spending in
41:1303:86550:18:18:72:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the data, the form of the adjustment costs cannot be identified from unconditional business
41:1304:86641:18:18:71:539:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cycle movements: quadratic adjustment costs andfixed costs of adjustment can produce
41:1305:86725:18:18:71:383:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exactly the same dampening of durable spending on average.
41:1306:86783:18:18:89:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:However, we now argue that the volatility of durable expendituresconditionalon the
41:1307:86865:18:18:71:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate state of the business cycle can provide additional identification that supports
41:1308:86954:18:18:71:539:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the presence offixed adjustment costs.  In particular, aggregate durable expenditures are
41:1309:87043:18:18:71:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:systematically more volatile during expansions than they are during slumps.  This arises
41:1310:87131:18:18:71:539:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:naturally in the model withfixed costs of durable adjustment, since we have shown that that
41:1311:87222:18:18:71:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model generates a procyclical IRF but not in models with convex adjustment costs. Beyond
41:1312:87310:18:18:71:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:supporting thefixed cost specification, we believe this result is interesting in its own right
41:1313:87404:18:18:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for optimal policy design.  Since policies are not implemented randomly over the business
41:1314:87493:18:17:71:539:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cycle, conditional responses are likely to be more informative for the effects of policy than
41:1315:87586:17:18:71:215:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:are unconditional responses.
41:1316:87614:18:18:89:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:To show that the volatility of durable expenditures rises during booms, we follow Bach-
41:1317:87701:18:18:71:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:mann, Caballero, and Engel [2013] and estimate a two-stage time-series model.  In thefirst
41:1318:87791:18:18:71:539:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:stage, we estimate an AR process for durable expenditures.  Then, in the second stage,
41:1319:87877:18:18:71:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:we regress the absolute value of the residuals from thefirst stage on the average of lagged
41:1320:87968:18:18:71:539:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures to assess whether residual variance is different during booms than it
41:1321:88058:18:18:71:540:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is during recessions.  (See Appendix 6 for details).  Wefind clear evidence that aggregate
41:1322:88148:18:18:71:539:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures exhibit conditional heteroscedasticity, with durable expenditures ex-
41:1323:88238:18:18:71:539:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:hibiting much larger (absolute) residuals following expansions.  Figure 17 shows that our
41:1324:88327:18:18:71:539:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:estimates of residual variance rise dramatically with previous durable expenditures.58At
41:1325:88415:18:18:72:540:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the peak of the nineties boom (when durable investment rates were very high), the residual
41:1326:88505:18:18:72:540:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:variance was 50% larger than at the trough of the 2007 recession (when durable investment
41:1327:88594:18:18:72:186:241:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:rateswereverylow).59
41:1328:88614:18:17:89:539:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In principle, conditional heteroscedasticity could arise for two reasons: (1) The economy
41:1329:88703:17:18:71:539:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is subject to shocks of constant variance but durable expenditures respond more to these
41:1330:88791:18:16:81:539:188:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:57Since we only pick two adjustment cost parameters, we can directly target the volatility of durable and
41:1331:88896:16:12:72:539:172:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:capital investment, and we get a slightly different number for the volatility of non-durable consumption.
41:1332:89001:12:12:72:539:160:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:(But this value is close enough that again it would not provide any direct identification of the adjustment
41:1333:89108:12:8:72:152:148:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:cost specification).
41:1334:89128:8:12:81:317:140:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:58Bootstrapped 90 percent confidence interval in gray.
41:1335:89182:12:16:81:539:128:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:59Regressing the second stage on other measures of the business cycle produces similar results but is less
41:1336:89288:16:12:72:539:112:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:parsimonious and requires taking a stand on exactlyhow we measure the business cycle in our model.  The
41:1337:89391:12:12:72:539:100:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:lagged durable investment rate should pick up all shocks that affect the level of households’ desired durable
41:1338:89500:12:0:72:111:88:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:holdings.
42:1339:89511:0:328:199:413:574:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:Figure 17: Conditional Heteroscedasticity

42:1347:89605:282:0:275:351:237:92:Helvetica:92:Helvetica:A:Average Lagged Id/D
43:1348:89644:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks during booms than during recessions. (2) The size of shocks during booms is greater
43:1349:89734:18:18:72:282:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:than the size of shocks during recessions.
43:1350:89776:18:18:89:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Appendix 6 shows that while durable expenditures exhibit conditional heteroscedasticity,
43:1351:89864:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:there is no evidence for heteroscedasticity for either productivity or monetary shocks. Thus,
43:1352:89957:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:there is no evidence for heteroscedasticity among the most common shocks used in business
43:1353:90046:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cycle models. Furthermore, aggregate GDP also does not exhibit conditional heteroscedas-
43:1354:90134:18:18:72:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ticity, and since the aggregate shocks affecting durable expenditures and total GDP should
43:1355:90224:18:18:71:544:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:be similar, we interpret conditional heteroscedasticity of durable expendituresasevidence
43:1356:90313:18:18:72:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of thefirst explanation:  durable expenditures become more responsive to aggregate shocks
43:1357:90402:18:18:72:220:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:during business cycle booms.
43:1358:90430:18:18:89:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Since the model withfixed costs of adjustment implies procyclical responsiveness while
43:1359:90516:18:18:72:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the model with convex adjustment costs does not, the aggregate time-series evidence thus
43:1360:90604:18:18:72:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:supports the former model.  Indeed, Appendix 6 shows that the model withfixed costs im-
43:1361:90691:18:17:72:540:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:plies conditional heteroscedasticity that is highly significant and in-line with the aggregate
43:1362:90785:17:18:72:540:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:data while the model with convex adjustment costs generates no conditional heteroscedas-
43:1363:90873:18:18:72:540:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ticity.   In addition, Berger and Vavra [2014] provide additional time-series evidence for
43:1364:90963:18:18:72:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:procyclical durable spending responsiveness.  In that paper, we use an STVAR to estimate
43:1365:91051:18:18:72:540:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the durable spending multiplier in response to identified government spending changes and
43:1366:91140:18:69:72:327:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:show that it rises dramatically during expansions.
43:1367:91190:69:29:72:213:316:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:7Conclusion
43:1368:91201:29:18:72:540:287:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In this paper, we argue that household-level durable adjustment frictions matter for aggregate
43:1369:91295:18:18:72:540:269:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:dynamics.  We use a novel indirect inference procedure to estimate an incomplete markets
43:1370:91383:18:18:72:539:251:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:model withfixed costs of durable adjustment and show that it does a very good job of
43:1371:91467:18:18:71:540:233:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:explaining various microeconomic consumption patterns.   More importantly, this model
43:1372:91552:18:18:71:539:215:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:implies that as household wealth and income falls during a recession, fewer households adjust
43:1373:91645:18:18:71:539:197:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:their durable holdings or are on the margin of doing so.  This means that the elasticity of
43:1374:91736:18:18:71:530:179:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate durable expenditures to shocks which affect durable demand falls substantially.
43:1375:91825:18:18:89:539:161:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We provide support for this mechanism in various ways.  In addition to showing that
43:1376:91908:18:18:71:539:143:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the average frequency of durable adjustment indeed falls in recessions, we show that cross-
43:1377:91999:18:18:71:539:125:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sectional distributions in the PSID data move as predicted by our model and that aggregate
43:1378:92089:18:18:71:539:107:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures are less responsive to reduced form time-series shocks during recessions.
43:1379:92183:18:18:89:540:89:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our results have implications for estimating the efficacy of durable stimulus.  The re-
43:1380:92270:18:0:71:540:71:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sponse of durable expenditures to changes in policy is highly dependent on the aggregate
44:1381:92360:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:state of the economy, which means that using estimates from linear VARs to estimate the
44:1382:92447:18:18:72:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:effects of any such program is likely to be misleading.  While a growing body of research
44:1383:92536:18:18:72:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:argues that the government spending multiplier should be countercyclical,60the forces we
44:1384:92624:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:identify push in the opposite direction.  In Berger and Vavra [2014] we provide STVAR
44:1385:92709:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:evidence that while the overall government spending multiplier is indeed countercyclical, the
44:1386:92802:18:18:72:502:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:"durable spending" multiplier is instead procyclical, just as predicted by our model.
44:1387:92887:18:18:89:539:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In this paper, we emphasized the general mechanism that causes micro adjustment fric-
44:1388:92972:18:18:72:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tions to lead to procyclical IRFs. As such, we considered a variety of aggregate shocks and
44:1389:93063:18:18:72:539:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:explored a very broad definition of durables that should include all durable goods subject
44:1390:93153:18:18:72:540:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to transaction costs of adjustment.  In future work, we plan to explore our model impli-
44:1391:93241:18:18:72:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cationsforparticularpoliciessuchasthe"Cash-for-Clunkers" program or the "First-Time-
44:1392:93325:18:18:72:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Homebuyer" credit.  Realistic policy analysis will require enriching our model to include
44:1393:93414:18:18:72:540:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:various institutional details that are beyond the scope of this paper. Nevertheless, our mod-
44:1394:93507:18:17:72:539:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:eling insights should continue to apply and we hope to quantify their importance for specific
44:1395:93600:17:18:72:540:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:policies.  For example, Mian and Sufi[2012] use cross-sectional variation in the propensity
44:1396:93691:18:18:72:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of clunkers to estimate the average effect of the "Cash-for-Clunkers" program, but our model
44:1397:93783:18:18:71:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:also implies that the effects of the policy should differ geographically with the distribution
44:1398:93877:18:18:71:539:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of wealth and local economic conditions.  More generally, understanding durable spending
44:1399:93965:18:18:71:539:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:patterns requires understanding the level and distribution of wealth in an economy and how
44:1400:94055:18:28:71:253:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this distribution moves across time.
44:1401:94091:28:0:81:278:339:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:60Due to, e.g., excess capacity or to the ZLB.

48:1472:98528:0:35:72:470:708:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:8  Appendix 1: Data Definitions and Cleaning
48:1473:98572:35:37:72:187:673:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:8.1  PSID Data
48:1474:98586:37:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:This appendix discusses provides additional discussion of our PSID data analysis.   We
48:1475:98672:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:restrict our analysis to 1999-2011 because prior to 1999, the PSID did not collect the data
48:1476:98763:18:18:72:540:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:necessary for our analysis.   Beginning in 1999, the PSID contains detailed information
48:1477:98850:18:18:72:545:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:onnon-durableconsumption,thevalueofhousingandvehiclesaswellasvariouswealth
48:1478:98924:18:18:72:540:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:holdings.  Although more detailed non-durable consumption data is available beginning in
48:1479:99012:18:18:72:540:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2003, for comparability we use only variables that are available beginning in 1999. The value
48:1480:99105:18:18:72:540:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for non-durable expenditures is the sum of all components of food consumption, utilities,
48:1481:99194:18:18:72:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:transportation expenses, schooling expenses and health services. Our measure of−1is the
48:1482:99282:18:17:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sum of last periods housing value and vehicle values.  Assets are the sum of business value,
48:1483:99374:17:18:71:390:475:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:stocks, iras, cash, bonds, minus the value of outstanding debt.
48:1484:99437:18:18:89:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our benchmark analysis is restricted to home-owners with household headage 65.
48:1485:99516:18:18:72:540:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:After constructing each of our variables, we deflate these nominal values using NIPA price
48:1486:99606:18:18:72:539:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:indices and remove a householdfixed effect.  To define durable adjustment, we combine
48:1487:99691:18:18:72:539:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:several questions in the PSID.  In our benchmark results, we define durable adjustment
48:1488:99777:18:18:72:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as a self-reported house or vehicle sale together with a 20% change in the reported value
48:1489:99866:18:18:72:540:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of the durable stock. We use a combination of self-reported adjustment and a minimum
48:1490:99950:18:18:72:540:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:threshold for several reasons.  1) Combining these indicators is likely to reduce spurious
48:1491:100040:18:18:72:540:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustments due to measurement error.  2) Some house sales are likely to be the results
48:1492:100127:18:18:72:540:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of idiosyncratic moves across location which may not lead to any substantial adjustment in
48:1493:100217:18:18:72:540:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the size of the stock. 3) Finally, and most importantly, self-reported adjustment indicators
48:1494:100309:18:18:72:540:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ask about adjustment over the previous three years while the sample is conducted every
48:1495:100395:18:18:72:540:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:two years.  This implies that the same adjustment may be counted twice.  Requiring a
48:1496:100479:18:18:72:540:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:simultaneous change in value and self-reported adjustment reduces this concern. We chose
48:1497:100567:18:17:72:539:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a 25% threshold because the median change inthe reported durable stock conditional on
48:1498:100652:17:18:72:540:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:self-reported adjustment is 40% while the median change conditional on no adjustment is
48:1499:100739:18:18:72:540:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:4%, so a 20% threshold roughly splits this distance. This adjustment definition generates an
48:1500:100831:18:18:72:274:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adjustment probability of roughly 10%.
48:1501:100869:18:18:89:540:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 1 applies this adjustment definition to our broad measure of durables that includes
48:1502:100959:18:18:72:540:134:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:housing and vehicles as well as to a more narrow definition that focuses just on housing after
48:1503:101053:18:18:71:539:116:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:removing deterministic age effects.   We split the sample in 1999 for the housing series
48:1504:101141:18:18:71:539:98:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:because the sampling frequency and thus questions change slightly and there appears to be
48:1505:101230:18:39:71:539:80:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a trend break in the series.  Table A1 reports results a for a panel logit for the probability
48:1506:101324:39:0:300:312:41:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:47
49:1507:101326:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of adjustment on recession indicators. Overall, the probability of broad durable adjustment
49:1508:101417:18:18:72:540:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:falls by around 20% during recessions while the probability of buying/selling a house falls
49:1509:101508:18:31:72:153:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:by around 15%.

49:1523:102382:18:31:71:308:388:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to a variety of location, time and age controls.

50:1585:104705:18:18:71:539:125:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:hicle stock is available annually beginning in 1990 and is available everyfive years before
50:1586:104796:18:18:71:539:107:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:1990.  To construct annual measures of vehicle registration before 1990 we use a perpetual
50:1587:104886:18:18:71:539:89:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inventory method.  For example, we observe the stock of vehicles in 1985 and 1990 and we
50:1588:104974:18:0:71:539:71:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:observe total purchases in each year from 1985-1990.  We assume that there is a constant
51:1589:105064:0:18:72:539:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:depreciation rate over eachfive year period and we pick this depreciation rate so that the
51:1590:105154:18:18:71:399:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:beginning and ending stock is consistent with annual purchases.
51:1591:105217:18:18:89:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The bottom panel of Figure , we merge data from HUD and the census.  HUD reports
51:1592:105297:18:18:71:297:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:data on existing home sales from 1969-2008:
51:1593:105340:18:18:89:548:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:((http://www.huduser.org/periodicals/ushmc/fall09/hist_data.pdf), which we merge with
51:1594:105425:18:18:71:388:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:data from the national association of realtors for recent years:

51:1599:105758:18:18:89:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In our time-series analysis in Section 6, we define durable expenditures as real consumer
51:1600:105847:18:18:71:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures + real residential investment where real consumer durables are NIPA
51:1601:105935:18:18:71:539:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Table 1.1.5 line 4 divided by NIPA Table 1.1.9 line 4 and real residential investment is NIPA
51:1602:106028:18:17:71:539:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:table 1.1.5 line 12 divided by NIPA Table 1.1.9 line 12. Non-durable consumption is defined
51:1603:106119:17:18:71:539:457:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as non-durable goods (NIPA Table 1.1.5 line 5 divided by NIPA Table 1.1.9 line 5) + services
51:1604:106211:18:18:71:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(Table 1.1.5 line 6 divided by Table 1.1.9 line 6) - housing services (Table 2.3.5 line 14 divided
51:1605:106309:18:18:71:540:421:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:by Table 2.4.4 line 14). Our measure of GDP is then the sum of non-durable consumption,
51:1606:106396:18:18:71:385:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable expenditures and private non-residential investment..
51:1607:106457:18:18:89:539:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We have also experimented with using analogous constructions with chained GDP rather
51:1608:106541:18:18:71:539:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:than constructing real GDP with the GDP deflator.  However, the necessary chained GDP
51:1609:106626:18:18:71:539:349:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:components are only available going back to 1995.  Nevertheless, the results for the most
51:1610:106715:18:18:71:539:331:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:recent recession are similar. In addition, it should be noted that due to the construction of
51:1611:106808:18:18:71:540:313:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the price deflators, the real series constructed by deflating the nominal series individually do
51:1612:106904:18:18:71:539:295:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:not add up to the aggregate real series. This problem is more problematic the further from
51:1613:106994:18:18:71:539:277:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the base year we move. Since the current NIPA data uses 2009 as the base year, this is likely
51:1614:107087:18:18:71:539:259:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to introduce only small errors into our results for the most recent recession, but it makes the
51:1615:107182:18:18:71:539:241:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:older series somewhat less reliable.  The businesscycle volatilities we estimate are sensitive
51:1616:107276:18:18:71:539:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to the exact procedure used to construct the individual consumption components (e.g. using
51:1617:107366:18:17:71:539:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:non-durable consumption + services - housing services to get our measure of non-durable
51:1618:107453:17:18:71:539:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:consumption does not obtain the exact same series as using PCE - housing services - durable
51:1619:107544:18:18:71:539:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:expenditures even though these two measures contain the same components).  These series
51:1620:107631:18:18:71:476:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:arenearlyidenticalinthe2000s,butdivergeaswemovefurtherbackintime.
51:1621:107696:18:18:89:539:134:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Constructing durable investment rates requires quarterly measures of the durable stock.
51:1622:107783:18:18:71:539:116:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Following Bachmann, Caballero, and Engel [2013], we construct measures of real annual
51:1623:107868:18:18:71:539:98:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durable stocks using nominal data from BEA Domestic Product and Income Tables 1.1.5 and
51:1624:107955:18:39:71:539:80:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:price deflators from Table 1.1.9.  We then next construct quarterly depreciation estimates
51:1625:108045:39:0:300:312:41:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:C:50
52:1626:108047:0:18:72:540:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:using annual nominal measures of depreciation from BEA Fixed Asset Table 1.1 together with
52:1627:108137:18:18:72:539:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the price deflators from Table 1.1.9. Since the BEA publishes annual measures of the stock of
52:1628:108230:18:18:72:540:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:durables and housing in Fixed Asset Table 1.1, we just need to construct quarterly measures
52:1629:108321:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in between these annual observations.  To do this, we combine the annual observations
52:1630:108406:18:18:72:540:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with the quarterly expenditure and depreciation measures together with a standard stock
52:1631:108493:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:accumulation expression to construct quarterly stock measures.  See Bachmann, Caballero,
52:1632:108581:18:57:72:326:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and Engel [2013] for the more detailed procedure.

52:1664:109655:18:0:71:539:95:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:=(1+)−1+−1(1−)−(1−)−1−so we can eliminate one state-variable
53:1665:109734:0:36:72:326:708:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and rewrite the value function when adjusting as:
53:1666:109783:36:10:135:298:672:145:g_d0_f9:145:g_d0_f6:C:e(−1; )=max
53:1667:109807:10:0:269:286:662:65:g_d0_f7:65:g_d0_f7:?:

53:1671:109849:20:21:266:282:649:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f5:C:

53:1673:109867:33:18:89:539:595:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Since the choice when adjusting is two-dimensional it takes substantially longer tofind
53:1674:109954:18:18:71:539:577:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the optimal policy for a given state than it does to solve for the policy when not adjust-
53:1675:110044:18:18:71:539:559:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ing.  Thus, eliminating a state-variable from this problem dramatically speeds calculations.
53:1676:110136:18:18:71:539:541:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Given these value functions, we approximatee(:;:)and(::;:)as
53:1677:110221:18:18:72:539:523:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:multilinear61functions in the continuous idiosyncratic states and one continuous aggregate
53:1678:110311:18:18:72:540:505:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:state. Initializing the grid for aggregate capital requires knowledge of the steady-state level
53:1679:110406:18:18:72:540:487:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of capital, so before solving the model with aggregate shocks, we solve for the steady-state
53:1680:110498:18:18:72:540:469:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of the model.  The solution method is similar and simpler than the solution with aggregate
53:1681:110588:18:18:72:266:451:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks, so we only describe the latter:
53:1682:110627:18:17:93:539:433:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Given an initial guess for the value functions and transition function, we solve for the
53:1683:110715:17:18:72:540:416:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:optimal two-dimensional policy functions using a Nelder-Meade algorithm initialized from
53:1684:110803:18:18:72:539:398:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:3different starting values to reduce the problems offinding local maxima in the policy
53:1685:110889:18:18:71:539:380:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:function.  The values of adjusting and not adjusting are compared, to generate the overall
53:1686:110979:18:18:71:539:362:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:policy function and to update the overall value function. We iterate until the separate value
53:1687:111072:18:18:71:540:344:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:functions change by less62than 0.001.  Once the value functions have converged, we then
53:1688:111159:18:18:71:539:326:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:solve for the optimal policy function an additional time on afiner grid, to use for simulation.
53:1689:111254:18:18:89:539:308:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We then simulate a panel of households and compute the evolution of the aggregate
53:1690:111335:18:18:71:553:290:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:capital stock to update the aggregate transition rule0=0()+1().Wethen
53:1691:111410:18:18:71:540:272:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:repeat the above procedure until the coefficients in the value function change by less than
53:1692:111501:18:18:71:539:254:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:1%.  Once the transition rule has converged, aggregate forecasts are highly accurate, with
53:1693:111591:18:18:71:539:236:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:20999.   We have experimented with including the aggregate durable stock in the
53:1694:111673:18:18:72:540:218:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:transition rule and found that it did little to improve forecasts, at considerable additional
53:1695:111766:18:18:72:173:200:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:computational cost.
53:1696:111785:18:17:89:539:182:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:For the benchmark results partial equilibrium results, we use 132 grid points each for
53:1697:111871:17:18:72:540:165:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:interpolating−1and−1, 100 grid points for approximating−1, and we discretize our
53:1698:111954:18:18:72:540:147:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shocks using 7 gridpoints for idiosyncratic productivity and 21 grid points for the aggregate
53:1699:112047:18:18:72:540:129:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:shock.  In the general equilibrium model, we use 25 grid points for interpolating−1and
53:1700:112134:18:16:81:539:111:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:61We have experimented with cubic spline interpolation and have found that the speed advantages of linear
53:1701:112239:16:12:71:540:95:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:interpolation appear to be worth potential decreases in accuracy (especially sincefixed costs imply that the
53:1702:112347:12:8:71:351:83:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:value functions may not be well approximated by cubic splines).
53:1703:112410:8:0:81:335:75:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:A:62Finer converge values didn’t appear to affect the results.
54:1704:112472:0:18:72:539:708:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:−1, 15 grid points for aggregate productivity, 7 points for idiosyncratic productivity and 5
54:1705:112565:18:18:72:232:690:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:grid points for interpolating.
54:1706:112596:18:18:89:539:672:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We construct afiner grid with 90 points for−1and−1to compute thefinal policy
54:1707:112674:18:18:72:540:654:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:function used for simulation in the GE model and a grid with 400 grid points for our partial
54:1708:112766:18:18:72:539:636:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium model.   Thus, ourfine policy function must be solved for approximately 3
54:1709:112851:18:18:72:540:618:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:million grid points in GE and their associated expectations.  In partial equilibrium, our
54:1710:112940:18:18:72:540:600:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:policy function uses almost 20 million grid points. (A large advantage of partial equilibrium
54:1711:113033:18:18:72:540:582:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is that since we need not solve for the aggregate transition rule, we can make the inner
54:1712:113121:18:18:72:540:564:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:solution of the model more accurate).  Our simulation uses 10,000 households for 3,000
54:1713:113207:18:18:72:302:546:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:periods with an initial burnin of 250 periods.
54:1714:113253:18:18:89:539:528:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In order to simulate U.S. time-series data and compute impulse response functions in our
54:1715:113341:18:18:72:540:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:models, we feed aggregate shocks into the model picked to match U.S. data.  For example,
54:1716:113429:18:18:72:540:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:if we want to calculate the impulse response of the economy to an income shock in 1990q1,

54:1719:113694:18:18:71:539:439:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f13:B:income shocks.  Then feed the model aggregate shocks19901  20134from19601−

54:1721:113882:18:18:72:540:403:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with the same sequence of shocks but assume that there is an additional 1% impulse to
54:1722:113967:18:18:72:540:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:income in 1990q1 which dies offat rate 0.87 and compute the sequence of investment rates
54:1723:114055:18:18:71:539:367:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:1990120134.  This delivers an estimate of the impulse response function to
